State v. Carr


A129427


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


215 Ore. App. 306; 170 P.3d 563; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1375


May 11, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
October 3, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Carr, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 89 (Or., Feb. 13, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
D045702M. Washington County Circuit Court. Mark Gardner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Washington County Circuit Court, Oregon, convicting him of criminal trespass in the second degree under Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.245, and sentencing him to five years' bench probation and 100 hours of community service.


OVERVIEW: The basis for the conviction was defendant's entering the grounds of a public school after the school's principal had told him not to enter. Defendant traveled to various schools in order to preach and to pass out religious literature to students as they arrived for classes. Defendant tried to position himself on the city sidewalk so that he was in the center of the area where the school buses arrived but was not directly in front of any of the bus doors. That location put defendant close to the arriving students but did not interfere with their access to the school. Defendant asserted that he was engaged in constitutionally protected conduct on public property and that any attempt to exclude him was unlawful. The appellate court ruled that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal under the First Amendment. The school grounds were not a public forum. The school used its property for school purposes, and defendant's activity was not part of that use. Unlike the sidewalk, the walkway between the school entrance and the sidewalk was not a public thoroughfare but was designed for those who were entering and leaving the school.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Marroquin


A127366


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


215 Ore. App. 330; 168 P.3d 1246; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1374



October 3, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
C041873CR. Washington County Circuit Court. Michael McElligott, Judge. On appellant's petition for reconsideration filed April 20, 2007; respondent's response to petition for reconsideration filed May 10, 2007; appellant's response to respondent's response to petition for reconsideration filed May 23, 2007. Disposition filed April 18, 2007. 212 Ore. App. 219, 157 P.3d 796.
State v. Marroquin, 212 Ore. App. 219, 157 P.3d 796, 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 590 (2007)



DISPOSITION: Reconsideration allowed; former disposition withdrawn; convictions on Counts 1-6 reversed and remanded; conviction on Count 8 affirmed; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Washington County Circuit Court, Oregon, convicted defendant of two counts of possession of a controlled substance, two counts of manufacture of a controlled substance, two counts of delivery of a controlled substance, and one count of tampering with physical evidence. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant petitioned for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, shortly after the appellate court's decision, the Oregon Supreme Court decided another case which he contended resulted in a change in the statutes or case law and required reversal of his convictions. The appellate court found that defendant failed to preserve a claim that admitting the laboratory report, without requiring the State to produce at trial the criminalist who prepared it or to demonstrate that that person was unavailable to testify, violated his right to confrontation. The appellate court concluded that, in light of the new case, the admission of the laboratory report, which confirmed that the substances seized from defendant's apartment were methamphetamine and cocaine, without requiring the State to produce at trial the criminalist who prepared the report or to demonstrate that the criminalist was unavailable, was obvious error under Or. Const. art. I, § 11. The appellate court chose to exercise its discretion to correct the trial court's error in admitting the crime laboratory report.


OUTCOME: Defendant's petition for reconsideration was allowed, and the former disposition withdrawn; defendant's convictions on Counts 1-6 were reversed and remanded; the conviction on Count 8 was affirmed, and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Travalini


A125604 (Control), A125605


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


215 Ore. App. 226; 168 P.3d 1159; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1332


May 30, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
September 26, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Travalini, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 125 (Or., Feb. 13, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
02CR0699; 03CR0865. Josephine County Circuit Court. Michael Newman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for arson in the first degree for intentionally damaging the property of another under Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.325(1)(a) (2003). Defendant moved for a judgment of acquittal. The Josephine County Circuit Court, Oregon, denied defendant's motion. Defendant was subsequently found guilty, sentenced, and ordered to pay $ 33,327.52 in restitution. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove past his ex-girlfriend's house and observed her new boyfriend's vehicle. Defendant drove to the rental house where he knew the new boyfriend lived and entered through an unlocked back door. Once inside, defendant found some flares. Defendant used two flares to set the house on fire. The resulting conflagration sent a dangerous amount of smoke and carbon monoxide into a small house approximately 14 feet from the back of the boyfriend's house and connected to it by a roof over a carport. At the time, nobody was in the boyfriend's house, but the second house was occupied. Although that occupant's property was damaged, she escaped without injury. The appellate court disagreed with defendant's argument that the mental state set out in the statute, "intentionally," carried over to the subcategory fact, and that because the State did not prove that he intended to cause serious physical injury, he should have been acquitted. An offense-subcategory fact was not an element of an offense to which a culpable mental state must apply by virtue of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 161.095(2) or 161.115(1), at least when the fact was not described in the statute itself.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dunlap

COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


215 Ore. App. 46; 168 P.3d 295; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1296

September 12, 2007, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Yamhill County, Oregon, convicted defendant of two counts of encouraging child sexual abuse in the second degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.686, and sentenced him to five years' probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court denied his motion to suppress evidence discovered as the result of the warrantless seizure and search of his computer; its denial of his motion to suppress statements that he made to his probation officer and other law enforcement officers; and its denial of his motion for judgments of acquittal on the charges. The appellate court found that defendant was afforded the opportunity to refuse to consent to the search of his computer. Nothing demonstrated that the officers' conduct preceding and surrounding the request to search created a sufficiently coercive environment so as to render defendant's consent involuntary. A factfinder could find beyond a reasonable doubt that the images were of actual children actually engaged in the conduct depicted. The evidence was sufficient to permit an inference that defendant had the required mental state.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

453 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Betnar


A127947


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


214 Ore. App. 416; 166 P.3d 554; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1142


March 16, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
August 15, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
031274. Clatsop County Circuit Court. George A. Van Hoomissen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Clatsop County Circuit Court, Oregon, of 199 counts of encouraging child sexual abuse in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.684, based on evidence that he duplicated or printed 199 sexually explicit images of children. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the statute under which he was convicted, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.684, violated his right to free expression under Or. Const. art. I, § 8. The instant court concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.684 did not punish expression. The dissemination of the depiction of the child sexual abuse was more than mere expression, but was further exploitative conduct that occurred after the abuse took place. The State was not required to prove that the underlying sexual abuse took place by proving when and where it occurred. Therefore, the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion for a judgment of acquittal on ex post facto grounds. The State's evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant duplicated or printed a photograph, videotape, or other visual record of sexually explicit conduct involving a child. The record showed that defendant was in possession of a computer that permitted the downloading and copying of images from the Internet or other sources. A rational trier of fact could infer that defendant himself printed or duplicated the images found in his possession. The trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress on timeliness grounds.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Nave


A129010


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


214 Ore. App. 324; 164 P.3d 1219; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1062


May 30, 2007, Submitted on Record and Briefs 
August 1, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Nave, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 1236 (Or., Dec. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
MI050240. Deschutes County Circuit Court. Barbara Haslinger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Deschutes County Circuit Court (Oregon), which permanently revoked his driving privileges after he pled guilty to driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUII), third offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to DUII. Because it was his third DUII conviction, the trial court permanently revoked his driving privileges pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 809.235(1)(b) (2003). On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 809.235(1)(b). The state argued that, because defendant pled guilty, the matter was not appealable. The court concluded that the matter was appealable. The court did not accept the premise of the State's argument that Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 limited a defendant to a challenge of a sentence. The State offered no argument in support of the suggestion that a revocation of driving privileges was not a "disposition" within the meaning of § 138.050(1). However, the court's opinion in Terry was controlling and adverse to defendant's arguments regarding the constitutionality of Or. Rev. Stat. § 809.235(1)(b). The court therefore concluded that the trial court did not err in permanently revoking defendant's driving privileges.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Hutchins


A128171


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


214 Ore. App. 260; 164 P.3d 318; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 1023


December 22, 2006, Argued and Submitted; June 7, 2007, Resubmitted En Banc 
July 25, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Hutchins, 344 Ore. 280, 180 P.3d 702, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 160 (2008)
Review dismissed by State v. Hutchins, 345 Ore. 690, 2009 Ore. LEXIS 232 (2009)
Review denied by State v. Hutchins, 2009 Ore. LEXIS 675 (Or., July 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
04C52451. Marion County Circuit Court. Claudia M. Burton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Marion County Circuit Court (Oregon), which convicted him of possession of a weapon by an inmate, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.275.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was an inmate, was moved to administration segregation after another prisoner was murdered. While he was away, the cell was searched and a hypodermic syringe was discovered. He was questioned about the syringe and gave an incriminating statement. After defendant was convicted, he sought review. In reversing, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.275 was unconstitutionally vague. The term "sharp instrument" passed constitutional muster because the individual terms were commonly used and relatively precise. Also, when the prosecution proved that defendant possessed a hypodermic needle, it proved that he possessed a weapon defined in § 166.275. However, the trial court erred when it denied defendant's motion to suppress his statements because they were obtained in violation of Or. Const. art. I, § 12. Here, defendant was being interrogated without the Miranda warnings. The particular circumstances of questioning here created an environment in which defendant felt compelled to answer. Defendant was not told where he was going, he was handcuffed and guarded during questioning, and he was never told that he could return to his cell.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded.

Butchart v. Baker County


A126840


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


214 Ore. App. 61; 166 P.3d 537; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 971


January 9, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
July 11, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
03827. Baker County Circuit Court. Warner V. Wasley, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment dismissing first and second claims vacated for lack of jurisdiction and remanded for entry of judgment dismissing those claims for lack of jurisdiction; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sued defendant county, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief from the county's declaration that it owned a road that ran across his property and asserting a claim for inverse condemnation. The Baker County Circuit Court (Oregon) rejected the landowner's claims. The landowner appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The county's decision to declare the road an RS 2477 road was a quasi-judicial decision, reviewable pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 34.010 to 34.102, where the county was obligated to make a discrete and particularized decision as to the road's status by virtue of its resolution to retain such rights-of-way. Moreover, the determination that the road satisfied the criteria was a closely circumscribed factual situation. The landowner was jurisdictionally precluded from seeking declaratory and injunctive relief because the writ of review statutes were the exclusive remedy for such claims, and he had failed to timely pursue a remedy via those statutes. Thus, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to consider the declaratory and injunctive relief claims. However, the inverse condemnation claim was for damages, and as such, it fell within the general jurisdiction of the trial court; Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.102 was not the exclusive remedy for that claim. The trial court's decision on the merits of the inverse condemnation claim was upheld as there was evidence supporting its decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the declaratory and injunctive relief claims was vacated for lack of jurisdiction. The case was remanded for entry of judgment dismissing those claims. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

State v. Terry


A129021


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


214 Ore. App. 56; 162 P.3d 372; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 982


May 30, 2007, Submitted on Record and Briefs 
July 11, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
210422808. Lane County Circuit Court. Jack A. Billings, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lane County Circuit Court (Oregon) convicting him of one count of driving under the influence of intoxicants, a violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.010. His sole contention on appeal was that the statute that defined the offense of which he was convicted violated his right to equal privileges and immunities guaranteed by Or. Const. art. I, § 20.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 809.235(1)(b) (2003) ran afoul of Or. Const. art. I, § 20, in that it treated persons differently on the basis of their residence. The court disagreed. The court noted that although residence might be a cognizable class for the purposes of Or. Const. art. I, § 20, it was not clear that the challenged statute treated persons differently on the basis of their residence. The statute distinguished on the basis of where the person committed the offense, not on the basis of where the person who committed the offense resided. Apart from that, however, it was clear that the class of persons who defendant contended were disadvantaged under the statute was not a "true class" under Or. Const. art. I, § 20. Defendant was responsible for having committed the offense on which he was being sentenced. Thus, the classification on which he relied was not based on factors that were beyond his control.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Papas v. Or. Liquor Control Comm'n


A129769


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


213 Ore. App. 369; 161 P.3d 948; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 852


January 19, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
June 13, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
OLCC-04-V-022, OLCC-04-V-022-A, OLCC-04-V-022-B. Oregon Liquor Control Commission.



DISPOSITION: Violation of OAR 845-006-0345(11)(c) reversed and remanded for reconsideration; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Oregon Liquor Control Commission (OLCC) issued a final order concluding that petitioners, a restaurant, its president, and its secretary, violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 471.360(1)(b) by mixing, serving, or selling alcoholic beverages without a license and violated Or. Admin. R. 845-006-0345(11)(c) by conducting drinking contests. Petitioners sought judicial review of the order.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant held stage shows on weekend nights in which the president drizzled a Greek liqueur into the open mouths of patrons while the crowd counted. The patron who continued drinking for the longest count won a T-shirt. In determining that petitioners violated Or. Admin. R. 845-006-0345(11)(c), OLCC in effect interpreted the rule to mean that conduct involving "competition" and "free pouring" constituted a drinking contest designed to increase consumption of alcohol in increased quantities, regardless of the licensees' intent in conducting such a contest or any measurement of the amounts consumed during the contest relative to amounts otherwise consumed. Under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.482(8)(a) and (c), the court determined that remand was necessary because OLCC's interpretation of the rule was inconsistent with the wording of the rule, particularly the plainly stated limitation as to which drinking contests were subject to the rule and the plain meanings of the words "increase" and "design." Nothing in OLCC's interpretation or application of the rule identified the consumption or quantities against which the required "increase" was to be, or was, measured.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to the drinking contest violation and remanded for reconsideration. The court otherwise affirmed.

Quimby v. Hill


A122861


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


213 Ore. App. 124; 159 P.3d 1264; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 743


October 23, 2006, Submitted on Record and Briefs 
May 30, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Quimby v. Hill, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 986 (Or., Oct. 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
02112419M. Malheur County Circuit Court. James R. Hargreaves, Senior Judge.
State v. Quimby, 182 Ore. App. 287, 48 P.3d 216, 2002 Ore. App. LEXIS 911 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his burglary and theft convictions were upheld on direct appeal, petitioner filed a petition for postconviction relief asserting various errors. Defendant corrections official's Or. R. Civ. P. 21(A)(8) motion to dismiss was granted. Petitioner filed an amended petition. The Malheur County Circuit Court (Oregon) granted the official's motion to strike the petition pursuant to Or. R. Civ. P. 23(A) and (D). Petitioner challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The lower court did not err in granting the motion to strike the amended petition in its entirety as petitioner had not sought permission to file the amended petition. Accordingly, the issue of whether the lower court would have been required to permit the filing of the amended petition at that time was not before the appellate court. In addition, petitioner had not assigned error to the denial of his subsequent written an oral requests to file an amended petition and as a result, that issue was not before the appellate court. Petitioner also offered no cogent reason why the lower court erred in striking the amended petition. The lower court did not err in striking the paragraph concerning the prosecution's attack of its own witness as Or. Evid. Code 607 permitted any party to attack a witness's credibility. The paragraph asserting several defects did not allege that counsel was ineffective and thus, they did not support an inadequate counsel claim. Those defects also could have been raised at trial or on direct appeal and petitioner failed to show any prejudice from the dismissal of that paragraph. The remaining assignments of error also lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

462 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnson


A124900


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


213 Ore. App. 83; 159 P.3d 1213; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 733


January 19, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
May 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Johnson, 343 Ore. 363, 169 P.3d 1268, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 825 (2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Johnson, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 598 (Or., Aug. 14, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
D0304188M. Washington County Circuit Court. Jon B. Lund, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant demurred to an indictment on the ground that Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.065(1)(a)(B) on its face violated the free expression guarantee in Or. Const. art. I, § 8. After the Washington County Circuit Court (Oregon) disallowed the demurrer, defendant was convicted of directing racist, obscene, and homophobic insults at the occupants of a car. Defendant challenged the conviction.


OVERVIEW: A prior version of the statute was held unconstitutional because it focused on expression instead of harm. The current statute shifted the focus from expression to conduct: No crime occurred unless harm, i.e., harassment or annoyance likely to provoke a violent response, occurred, albeit harm that was caused by expression. That type of harm was within the legislature's authority to prevent. The statute was not overly broad. To convict for the only type of speech intended and likely to cause a violent response that might have been privileged, inflammatory insults with political implications, the prosecution was required to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the epithet was intended and likely to provoke retaliatory violence from a specified individual. The finding that defendant's speech was intended and likely to provoke a violent response was affirmed where the evidence showed that he had used racial and other epithets over an amplified public address system, in stop-and-go traffic, for upward of five minutes. Moreover, a brief heated oral exchange had taken place. No physical violence had occurred, but only because the victim's companion had intervened.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed.

Richardson v. Driver & Motor Vehicle Servs. Div.


A130241


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


213 Ore. App. 18; 159 P.3d 1227; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 738


November 2, 2006, Argued and Submitted 
May 23, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Richardson v. Driver & Motor Vehicle Servs., 2008 Ore. LEXIS 15 (Or., Jan. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
120463. Department of Transportation.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for reconsideration of denial of permit; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individual sought judicial review of an order from the Driver and Motor Vehicle Services Division of the Oregon Department of Transportation (DMV) that cancelled the individual's driving privileges, denied further driving tests, and denied a request for a permit to take driving lessons.


OVERVIEW: The statutory and administrative standards for cancelling driving privileges were not unconstitutionally vague under Or. Const. art. I, §§ 20 and 21, as they reasonably cabined the DMV's discretion. The decision to cancel the individual's driving privileges did not lack substantial reason as the DMV made specific findings as to the driving errors made in three recent driving tests and based on those findings, concluded that she met Or. Admin. R. 735-062-0073(3). The individual had preserved the issue of whether the DMV erred in denying further testing where her attorney had expressly raised the issue at the hearing and the DMV had addressed the issue. However, the DMV did not err in denying the individual's ability to take a fourth driving test as its final order, when read in its entirety, showed that it had applied the correct standard, i.e., Or. Admin. R. 735-063-0073. Moreover, substantial evidence supported the DMV's finding that the standard was met. The DMV's refusal to issue a permit so that the individual could take driving lessons was reversed as it failed to explain why further driver training or driver rehabilitation should not have been made available.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and remanded for reconsideration to the extent that it denied the individual's request for a permit to take driving lessons, but was otherwise affirmed.

Spivak v. Marriott


A126249


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


213 Ore. App. 1; 159 P.3d 1192; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 737


August 21, 2006, Argued and Submitted 
May 23, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
040100327. Multnomah County Circuit Court. Jeffrey Kilmer, Judge pro tempore.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before his death, plaintiff decedent sued defendant agency and director, seeking a petition for a writ of review and alleging constitutional, conversion, and contract claims related to alleged sewer overpayments. The Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon) dismissed the petition pursuant to Or. R. Civ. P. 21A and granted defendants' motion for summary judgment on the remaining claims. Appellant personal representatives challenged the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The representatives were entitled to challenge the basis for the trial court's decision without having to show that the decedent preserved the same arguments below or that the trial court's error was plain on the face of the record where the trial court had invoked a new principle in deciding defendants' motions to dismiss, i.e., the decedent had not served a writ. Since the decedent did not have notice that service would be an issue, he had no opportunity to preserve any error. Thus, the parties were entitled to dispute the issue on appeal. The trial court erred in dismissing the petition for a writ of review for lack of jurisdiction where the decedent had filed it within the statutorily prescribed time, thereby giving the trial court jurisdiction. The decedent's failure to file the requisite undertaking was not a jurisdictional defect. Summary judgment was improper on the remaining claims where the condemnation and common law claims sought to enforce rights that would not necessarily be adjudicated on review of the agency's decision. Thus, it was premature to determine whether the remaining claims would be precluded by the adjudication of the writ of review claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded.

 

465 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Magana


A125662 (Control); A125663


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


212 Ore. App. 553; 159 P.3d 1163; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 714


July 11, 2006, Argued and Submitted 
May 16, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Magana, 343 Ore. 363, 169 P.3d 1268, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 842 (Oct. 18, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Magana v. State, 253 Ore. App. 478, 293 P.3d 235, 2012 Ore. App. LEXIS 1327 (Oct. 31, 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Magana v. Rosenblum, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 144896 (D. Or., May 22, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Lane County Circuit Court. Court Numbers 20-03-16714, 20-03-22888. Karsten H. Rasmussen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Lane County Circuit Court (Oregon) convicting him of numerous crimes, including multiple sex offenses, coercion, and official misconduct, and sentencing him to 975 months in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a former police officer, was convicted for telling the victims, women he met in the course of his duties, that he would not arrest or cite them if they would engage in sexual activity with him. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by disallowing defendant's demurrer to one of the indictments charging him with first-degree official misconduct and coercion on the ground that some of the counts lacked enough specificity to allow him to prepare a defense because the charges tracked the wording of the statutes defining official misconduct and coercion, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 162.415, 163.275. The fact that the charged crimes were complex, making the indictment difficult to defend against, did not make the indictment, worded using the statutory alternatives, fatally insufficient. The fact that the discovery was voluminous did not establish that it was insufficient to illuminate the indictment; the kind of discovery reasonably expected would include witness statements regarding what defendant did or failed to do, which would supply the requisite specificity.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State v. Brown


A124830


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


212 Ore. App. 164; 157 P.3d 301; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 530


December 21, 2006, Submitted on Record and Briefs 
April 18, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Brown, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 1052 (Or., Oct. 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
03CR0157. Coos County Circuit Court. Michael J. Gillespie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Coos County Circuit Court, Oregon, of rape in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.375. Defendant appealed, challenging the denial of his motion to suppress DNA evidence.


OVERVIEW: The rape was committed in 1998. In 2001, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.076, defendant was required to provide a buccal sample following his convictions for felonies. In 2002, the Oregon State Police crime laboratory compared the DNA that had been seized from the rape scene with the sample given by defendant in 2001 and determined that the samples matched. That discovery led to the issuance of a search warrant and the seizure of additional DNA from defendant. That evidence was admitted at trial. Defendant argued that the compelled taking of his DNA in 2001 pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.076 violated Or. Const. art. I, § 9 and the Fourth Amendment to the United States Constitution. Nevertheless, the procedure that occurred in this case was akin to the fingerprinting of a person in custody; therefore, the appellate court concluded that the seizure of defendant's DNA did not constitute an unreasonable seizure under either constitution. Defendant also filed a pro se supplemental brief, in which he challenged the imposition of a mandatory minimum sentence, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.700. Nevertheless, defendant conceded that he did not raise an objection in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

467 of 770 DOCUMENTS



Home Builders Ass'n v. City of Springfield


A129475 (Control), A129476


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


211 Ore. App. 658; 156 P.3d 167; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 490


November 22, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
April 4, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 16-04-15534; 16-04-15996. Lane County Circuit Court. Karsten H. Rasmussen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, developers, challenged the legality of the methodology for imposing system development charges (SDCs) adopted pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 223. After respondents, cities, adopted the methodology, developers sought review by the Lane County, Oregon, Circuit Court under Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.040. The trial court rejected the developers' challenges, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: The methodology at issue was intended to operate as the framework to fund improvements to wastewater treatment facilities. The appellate court had to determine whether the developers' challenges were properly reviewed by the trial court for substantial evidence or whether the trial court should have considered the issues raised by the developers as legal issues concerning statutory construction. The appellate court held that the issues, as framed by the developers, did not present issues of statutory interpretation because they did not raise questions of legislative intent regarding the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. § 223.304(1), (2). Rather, the statutes informed what a methodology for the assessment of improvement fees had to be based on. Although the developers disagreed with some of the factors relied on by the cities that formed the basis for the methodology, those kinds of determinations were used by experts in the field to formulate methodologies for assessing SDCs. Because those factors were factual in nature, they were properly subject to review for substantial evidence, and the trial court did not err in exercising its review authority under Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.040(1)(c).


OUTCOME: The decison of the circuit court was affirmed.

Dunn v. Hill


A130665


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


211 Ore. App. 590; 156 P.3d 72; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 410


January 5, 2007, Submitted on Record and Briefs  
March 28, 2007, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 05084588M. Malheur County Circuit Court. Richard D. Barber, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment dismissing writ reversed; order to pay $ 33 filing fee affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed from the Malheur County Circuit Court, Oregon, which dismissed his petition for writ of habeas corpus under Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.710. He claimed that the trial court erred in granting defendant superintendent's motion to dismiss the writ for failure to state a claim of denial of right of access to the courts, in denying the inmate's motion to amend his replication, and in ordering him to pay a $ 33 filing fee.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that the trial court erred in granting the superintendent's motion to dismiss the writ on the ground that the inmate's access to the courts claim failed to state a claim for relief. The inmate alleged that he had pending legal cases, including a post-conviction case, and that the superintendent's failure to maintain an adequate law library, and failure to allow him access to his pleadings and legal research stored on computer disk at the state penitentiary, had impeded his ability to meaningfully pursue those cases. The inmate also alleged that he was unable to adequately and meaningfully defend against the attorney general's pleadings which cited certain cases. Although the inmate did not identify the specific pleadings at issue, he did allege that the impediment affected his ability to respond to pleadings, not some other legal instrument. This was sufficient to allege that the inmate was deprived of a meaningful opportunity to present his claims to the court as required by the Constitution. Finally, the appellate court concluded that the inmate adequately alleged facts demonstrating that habeas corpus relief was the only adequate remedy practically available.


OUTCOME: The trial court erred in granting the superintendent's motion to dismiss the writ and the appellate court reversed the judgment. The appellate court affirm the trial court's order imposing a $ 33 filing fee.

 

469 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Luers


A115208


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


211 Ore. App. 34; 153 P.3d 688; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 240


November 30, 2005, Argued and Submitted  
February 14, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Modified by, Adhered to, Reconsideration granted by Or. v. Jeffrey Michael Luers, 213 Ore. App. 389, 160 P.3d 1013, 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 846 (Or. Ct. App., June 13, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of judgment reflecting single conviction for first-degree arson and single conviction for attempted first-degree arson; sentences vacated; remanded for resentencing; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), convicted defendant of three counts of first degree arson, two counts of attempted first degree arson, two counts of unlawful possession and two counts of unlawful manufacture of a destructive device, one count of first degree criminal mischief, and one count of attempted first degree criminal mischief, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 164.325 (1999), 161.405, 166.382, 166.384, 164.365, and 161.405. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Each of defendant's arson and attempted arson offenses violated only one statutory provision, namely Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.325(1)(b). That aspect of the appellate court's analysis weighed in favor of merger under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.067(1). Further, the circumstance at issue in each offense did not require proof of an element that the other circumstances did not. Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.067(1) did not preclude merger of defendant's three convictions for first-degree arson arising out of his conduct in setting the car dealership fire. By the same reasoning, that statute also did not preclude merger of defendant's two convictions for attempted arson arising out of the incident at the petroleum product supplier's truck yard. Also, for purposes of the two attempted arson convictions, the victim for each count was the same - the petroleum product supplier, who was the owner of the fuel truck that was the direct object of defendant's conduct. Thus, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.067(1) and (2), the trial court erred in failing to merge defendant's three arson convictions into a single conviction and in failing to merge his two attempted arson convictions into a single conviction.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for entry of a judgment reflecting a single conviction for first-degree arson and a single conviction for attempted first-degree arson. The appellate court vacated defendant's sentences and remanded the case for resentencing. Otherwise, the appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Cato v. Alcoa-Reynolds Metals Co. (In re Sworden)


A125705


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


210 Ore. App. 721; 152 P.3d 981; 2007 Ore. App. LEXIS 214


May 4, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
February 7, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Cato v. Alcoa-Reynolds Metals Co., 343 Ore. 115, 162 P.3d 988, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 610 (Or., June 19, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, the decedent's live-in girlfriend and his personal representative, sought review of a decision of the Workers' Compensation Board affirming the dismissal of petitioners' hearing requests.


OVERVIEW: The decedent applied for workers' compensation benefits after he was diagnosed with bladder cancer. Six months after the decedent's death, his former employer accepted his claim. In response, the decedent's personal representative, who was also his son with his girlfriend, requested a hearing in which he sought to set aside the acceptance on the ground of fraud. The girlfriend also sought a hearing, arguing that she was entitled to survivor's benefits. On appeal of the decision denying them hearings, the court affirmed. The court held that the decedent's girlfriend was not entitled to survivor benefits under Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.226 because the 24-year-old son she and the decedent had together was not, at the relevant time, under age 18 or otherwise dependent on the girlfriend for his support. The court further held that the personal representative did not have standing to request a hearing because Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.218(3), (5) limited that right to those who were entitled to death benefits, such as a surviving spouse, children under 18, or other dependent persons.


OUTCOME: The decision denying petitioners' requests for hearings was affirmed.

Christiansen v. Providence Health Sys. of Or. Corp.


A122603


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


210 Ore. App. 290; 150 P.3d 50; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 2017


March 10, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
December 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Christiansen v. Providence Health Sys. of Or. Corp., 343 Ore. 206, 166 P.3d 535, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 772 (2007)
Affirmed by Christiansen v. Providence Health Sys. of Or. Corp., 2008 Ore. LEXIS 276 (Or., May 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0301-00634. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Nely L. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the mother and conservator of the estate of her minor child, sought review of a judgment from the Multnomah County Circuit Court (Oregon) dismissing her medical negligence action against defendants, a hospital and an obstetrician, on the ground that the action was barred by the ultimate repose provision of Or. Rev. Stat. § 12.110(4).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that defendants failed to recognize signs of fetal distress during plaintiff's labor in March 1994 and negligently delayed performing a cesarean section delivery. Within six to eight months after the delivery, plaintiff suspected negligence but she contended that she did not learn of the child's permanent injuries until May 1999. The negligence action was filed in January 2003. The court agreed with the trial court that the statute of limitations under Or. Rev. Stat. § 12.160 did not begin to run based on plaintiff's mere suspicion of tortious conduct within six to eight months. Nevertheless, the court also agreed with the trial court that, notwithstanding § 12.160, the statute of ultimate repose under Or. Rev. Stat. § 12.110(4) barred plaintiff's claim because it was not brought within five years of March 1994. Because plaintiff would not have had an absolute common-law right to bring an action in negligence for the child's prenatal injuries in 1857 when the Oregon Constitution was adopted, the trial court properly ruled that the application of § 12.110(4) to plaintiff's claims did not violate the remedy clause of Or. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal.

State v. Tanner


A128680


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


210 Ore. App. 70; 150 P.3d 31; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1965


April 28, 2006, Argued and Submitted; Resubmitted En Banc October 19, 2006.  
December 20, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by, Review granted by State v. Tanner, 343 Ore. 554, 173 P.3d 831, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 1169 (2007)
Review denied by State v. Tanner, 2009 Ore. LEXIS 436 (Or., June 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9902-31447. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Kimberly C. Frankel, Senior Judge.
State v. Tanner, 192 Ore. App. 670, 87 P.3d 688, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 398 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), convicting him of, inter alia, robbery, rape, burglary, and kidnapping. The trial court imposed consecutive sentences totaling 616 months' imprisonment pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.123(5).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's charges arose from a continuous and uninterrupted course of conduct directed against two victims. Defendant argued the court's imposition of consecutive sentences pursuant to § 137.123(5) violated his right to a jury trial under U.S. Const. amend. VI through the Blakely and Apprendi rules. On appeal, the court found that the trial court's imposition of consecutive sentences did not violate the Sixth Amendment. Blakely and Apprendi concerned what facts were required to be found by a jury in order to impose a sentence that exceeded the statutory maximum for a single offense and involved a court's usurpation of factfinding traditionally performed by juries. Apprendi and Blakely did not address multiple sentences running consecutively, and the determination to impose concurrent or consecutive sentences was not a traditional jury function. Thus, although Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.123(5) did require the court to make findings of fact, it did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Drayton v. DOT


A113350 (Control), A113351, A113352 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


209 Ore. App. 656; 149 P.3d 331; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1925


October 6, 2006, Submitted on Remand  
December 13, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 74385, 85901, 86367. On remand from the Oregon Supreme Court, Drayton v. Dept. of Transportation, 341 Ore. 244, 142 P.3d 72 (2006). Judicial Review from Department of Transportation.
Drayton v. DOT, 341 Ore. 244, 142 P.3d 72, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 1012 (2006)
Drayton v. DOT, 186 Ore. App. 1, 62 P.3d 430, 2003 Ore. App. LEXIS 98 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Final orders in A113351 (Case No. 85901) and A113352 (Case No. 86367) reversed and remanded for reconsideration as to signs at milepoints 112.40, 112.42, and 112.46; final orders in A113350 (Case No. 74385), A113351 (Case No. 85901), and A113352 (Case No. 86367) reversed as to signs at milepoints 112.45, 114.41, and 118.43.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged orders by the Oregon Department of Transportation (department) requiring removal of six outdoor advertising signs. The court reversed and remanded for reconsideration with respect to three of the signs, and affirmed as to the other three signs. The Oregon Supreme Court remanded the case for reconsideration in light of its holding that certain provisions of the Oregon Motorist Information Act (OMIA) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court's original decision to reverse the department's orders with respect to three of the signs was based on the failure of the department to provide adequate notice to petitioner. That holding was unaffected by the subsequent Oregon Supreme Court's decision. The court's original decision, however, also affirmed the department's final orders with respect to the remaining three signs, and that part of the court's decision had to be reversed. With respect to each of those signs, the department predicated its determination that the signs were unlawful on its conclusions that (1) each of the signs was an "outdoor advertising sign" within the meaning of the OMIA because it advertised goods and services that were located off the premises, and (2) petitioner had erected and maintained the signs without obtaining the permits required by the OMIA for such signs. Because the Oregon Supreme Court had struck down the permitting requirements for "outdoor advertising signs" that formed the basis for the department's conclusion that petitioner's signs were unlawful, the court concluded that the department erred in concluding that petitioner was required to obtain such permits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for reconsideration with respect to three of the signs, and reversed the department's order with respect to the remaining three.

Groth v. Hyundai Precision & Ind. Co.


A121714


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


209 Ore. App. 781; 149 P.3d 333; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1927; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,642

December 13, 2006, Filed

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff personal representative sued defendants, a car manufacturer, a machine company, and a distributor, alleging a wrongful death claim. Defendants appealed the denial of their motions for a directed verdict and for a new trial by the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon). The personal representative cross-appealed the award of noneconomic damages.


OVERVIEW: The action was brought by the personal representative on behalf of the estate of a machinist who was killed while operating a vertical industrial lathe at the manufacturer's facility. Barrett v. Belleque


A127929


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


209 Ore. App. 295; 150 P.3d 1064; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1779


December 2, 2005, Submitted on Record and Briefs  
November 15, 2006, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which sua sponte denied, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.370(6), his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that he was transferred to the Intensive Management Unit (IMU) at a correctional institution as additional punishment for a fight and assault on a corrections officer. The inmate's theory was that placement in the IMU constituted punishment--a deprivation of a constitutionally protected liberty interest--and that he was entitled to a hearing before being assigned to that unit. The trial court stated that there was no constitutional right to placement outside the IMU. On appeal, the court did not reach the merits of the inmate's constitutional argument because the court concluded that he was not entitled to raise his challenge in a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The court noted that cases in which courts concluded that habeas corpus was the only appropriate remedy generally involved ongoing concerns about health or safety. The inmate neither challenged the conditions of confinement in the IMU as violating his constitutional rights, nor did he assert that he was suffering from dangerous or unhealthy conditions. The court noted that his procedural challenges to his IMU assignment could have been brought as a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 02-01950; Judicial Review from Workers' Compensation Board.
Ellison v. Weyerhaeuser (In re Ellison), 193 Ore. App. 635, 91 P.3d 815, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 682 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of an order of the Oregon Workers' Compensation Board, which, on remand, determined that the correct rate for the calculation of respondent claimant's scheduled permanent disability was $ 511.29 per degree.


OVERVIEW: The issue in dispute was the "date of injury" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.202(2) for purposes of determining the claimant's benefits for a hearing loss. The employer argued that the date of injury was a question that was raised or raiseable at the time of a stipulation reached between the parties and that the claimant was precluded from disputing that issue. The court concluded that the Board correctly found that the date of injury was not an issue that was resolved by the stipulation. The claimant was entitled to challenge the processing of the claim if it failed to result in benefits provided by law. Thus, the claimant's challenge to the date of injury stated in the notice of closure was not precluded by the stipulation. The court also concluded that Oregon's Contracts Clause, Or. Const. art. I, § 21, was not implicated by its interpretation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 656.202(2), relating to the meaning of the "date of injury." The court's interpretation also did not impair a contractual relationship within the meaning of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 1.


OUTCOME: The Board's decision was affirmed.

State v. Miller


A127389


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 424; 144 P.3d 1052; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1510


July 31, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
October 4, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Adhered to, Reconsideration granted by State v. Miller, 210 Ore. App. 176, 149 P.3d 1251, 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 2001 (Or. Ct. App., Dec. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 03CR0968. Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Allan H. Coon, Senior Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Josephine County (Oregon), which agreed with defendant that lab reports were inadmissible without the live testimony of the criminalist who prepared the reports and which concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.235 was unconstitutional and which therefore excluded the lab reports in the prosecution of defendant for possession of a controlled substance, Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.992 (2003).


OVERVIEW: The State moved in limine to determine the admissibility of two lab reports prepared by the state police forensic laboratory. The State wished to introduce the reports into evidence without calling the authors of those reports as witnesses. In the reports, defendant was denominated as a suspect due to a toxicological examination of defendant's urine specimen, which confirmed the presence of methamphetamine. The trial court agreed with defendant that the reports were inadmissible without the live testimony of the authors of the reports. On appeal, the court agreed that the trial court's ruling to exclude the reports was correct. The court determined that the reports were testimonial for purposes of Sixth Amendment analysis. The court concluded that a lab report that was prepared by staff at a state crime laboratory at the request of police for use in a criminal prosecution of a specific defendant would not fall within the shop book rule exception to the hearsay rule. The court disagreed with the trial court that Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.235 was unconstitutional, but it noted that defendant elected to have the State call the authors of the lab reports, and the State did not do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

AFT-Oregon v. Or. Taxpayers United Pac


A122158 (Control), A122168 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 350; 145 P.3d 1111; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1523; 180 L.R.R.M. 3174


September 20, 2005, Argued and Submitted  
October 4, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Adhered to, Reconsideration granted by AFT-Or. v. Or. Taxpayers United Pac, 209 Ore. App. 518, 149 P.3d 159, 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1896 (Or. Ct. App., Dec. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0108-08942, 0012-12632. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Jerome E. LaBarre, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment against Oregon Taxpayers United PAC on Count 3 reversed; paragraphs 6 and 9 of judgment reversed; paragraph 13 reversed as to Oregon Taxpayers United PAC; paragraph 7 vacated as to Oregon Taxpayers United PAC and remanded; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a political action committee (PAC) and a taxpayer organization, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) in favor of plaintiffs, an education association, a teachers association and intervenor State in an action pursuant to the Oregon Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act (ORICO), Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.715 to 166.735. Monetary damages and equitable relief were awarded.


OVERVIEW: The jury found that defendants had engaged in a pattern of racketeering activity in connection with forged sponsorship signatures for two initiative measures that would have restricted the ability of school districts to implement check-offs for payroll deductions for union dues. The court reversed in part and held that the existence of "an application" was the sine qua non of culpability under Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.085(1). Regarding the PAC's status as a political committee, there was no "application." Because there was no "application," the PAC's submissions could not have been made in connection with an application for any benefit. Therefore, the trial court erred in denying the motion to dismiss the § 162.085(1) count as to the PAC. The taxpayer organization's submissions of the false statements were properly not dismissed because they were material to its continuing eligibility and beneficial entitlement to engage in fund-raising activities in Oregon. Also, the trial court properly denied defendants' motion to dismiss under Or. R. Civ. P. 21 A(8). Further, the denial of defendants' summary judgment motion was not reviewable on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment against the PAC on the Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.085(1) claims were reversed. The injunction against the PAC was reversed. The court otherwise affirmed.

State v. Nordloh


A121786


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 309; 144 P.3d 1013; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1469


March 24, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
September 27, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 02CR0667. Appeal from Circuit Court, Josephine County. Allan H. Coon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Josephine County Circuit Court, Oregon, which convicted her of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: A traffic control officer stopped defendant's vehicle for making an unsignaled turn. After determining that defendant's driving privileges were suspended and that she did not have automobile insurance, the officer cited defendant and impounded her vehicle. The officer conducted an inventory search of the vehicle's contents pursuant to the police department's policy, which required that all impounded vehicles be inventoried. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying her motion to suppress evidence of contraband seized from her car pursuant to the department's inventory policy. The instant court concluded that the inventory violated Or. Const. art. I, § 9. The power to inventory a vehicle's contents could only be conducted pursuant to a properly authorized policy. Because the department's inventory policy required the officer to open all closed containers in the impounded vehicle, it was not reasonably related to protecting property or eliminating false claims. Thus, the purported inventory that was conducted pursuant to the policy was a warrantless and nonconsensual search requiring suppression of the evidence found during the inventory.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

480 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Krueger


A122970 (Control), A122971 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 166; 144 P.3d 1007; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1471


February 22, 2006, Submitted on Record and Briefs  
September 27, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0208-48646, 0211-53303. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Merri Souther Wyatt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Multnomah County, Oregon, convicted defendant for unlawful prostitution activities, Portland, Or., City Code (PCC) 14A.40.050. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that PCC 14A.40.050 was unconstitutional because it was preempted by state statute and was impermissibly vague. The appellate court found that the challenged ordinance did not prohibit what the state statutes, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 161.405 and 167.007(1), permitted. The State was correct that the ordinance and the statutes prohibited the same conduct. Even if defendant were correct, the fact that a state statute did not expressly prohibit conduct did not establish that the state statute affirmatively permitted that conduct. The legislature did not intend affirmatively to permit actions that were prohibited by PCC 14A.40.050. The ordinance quite unambiguously prohibited the behavior engaged in by defendant, and, as a result, defendant was precluded from bringing a facial vagueness challenge. Each of the terms at issue was clearly tied to conduct committed in a manner manifesting a particular intent, in this case, an intent to induce, entice, solicit, procure, locate, or contact another person to commit an act of prostitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

481 of 770 DOCUMENTS



Lake County v. Teamsters Local Union #223


A126592


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 271; 145 P.3d 187; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1477


July 20, 2005, Argued and Submitted, Resubmitted En Banc June 7, 2006.  
September 27, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ERB UC-9-04. Judicial review from Employment Relations Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county sought judicial review from an order of the Oregon Employment Relations Board (ERB), which held that a county employee was not a "confidential employee" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.650(6). The matter commenced when respondent union filed a petition for clarification of the public employee status of the county employee.


OVERVIEW: The union argued that the county did not exhaust its administrative remedies and that the court was precluded from considering the county's arguments. The court disagreed, but it noted that merely because the county exhausted its administrative remedies did not mean that it could consider all of the arguments that the county raised on judicial review. The court first declined to consider the county's argument that, by adding the word "necessary," ERB made § 243.650(6) impossibly and unconstitutionally vague. The constitutionality of § 243.650(6) was not raised below and the county therefore did not preserve its argument. The court also declined to consider the county's argument that ERB improperly added the word "necessary" to the definition of confidential employee in § 243.650(6) and that the addition of "necessary" to § 243.650(6) violated principles of statutory interpretation. The court determined that the county invited that purported error by statements it made in its closing argument to the administrative law judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.


 

482 of 770 DOCUMENTS



Dew v. City of Scappoose


A123026


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 121; 145 P.3d 198; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1508


October 3, 2005, Argued and Submitted  
September 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Dew v. City of Scappoose, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 115 (Or., Feb. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 01-2080. Appeal from Circuit Court, Columbia County. Sidney A. Galton, Judge.
Dew v. City of Scappoose, 202 Ore. App. 327, 124 P.3d 234, 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 1388 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment on second claim against Huffman and on first, third, fourth, and sixth claims against City of Scappoose reversed and remanded; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, former police chief of appellee city, challenged the decision of the Circuit Court, Columbia County (Oregon), which granted the city's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the action against appellee city councilor in the chief's action that arose out of the termination of her employment, including complaints under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and former Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 659.510(2), 659.530 (1999).


OVERVIEW: The councilor was a practicing criminal defense attorney, and the chief asserted that the councilor attempted to use his position to benefit his law practice. The chief's employment was terminated after some outbursts, including the throwing of furniture. The chief settled only her intentional interference claim against the councilor. The court reversed in part and held that the claims disposition agreement executed between the chief and the workers' compensation carrier did not operate as a release of all claims because many of the chief's claims did not arise out of the workers' compensation claim itself. Also, because the city did not raise the affirmative defense of insufficient service of process, it waived that defense. Further, a reasonable factfinder could find that the decision had been made to terminate the chief by the time of the chair-throwing incident, and there was conflicting evidence about the city council's involvement in the termination decision. Therefore, there were triable issues on the § 1983 claim. The Or. Rev. Stat. § 659.510 claim was barred by the statute of limitations, but the wrongful discharge claim was an exception to the at-will employment rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment on the § 1983 claim against the councilor and on the § 1983, wrongful discharge, former Or. Rev. Stat. § 659.436, and former Or. Rev. Stat. § 659.410 (1999) claims against the city were reversed. The court otherwise affirmed.

State v. Jacob


A119971


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


208 Ore. App. 62; 145 P.3d 212; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1467


March 30, 2005, Argued and Submitted; Resubmitted En Banc July 12, 2006.  
September 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Jacob, 342 Ore. 644, 158 P.3d 507, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 392 (2007)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Jacob, 344 Ore. 181, 180 P.3d 6, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 59 (2008)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Dismissed by, Request denied by, Certificate of appealability denied Jacob v. Persson, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 6500 (D. Or., Jan. 20, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0202-31253. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Robert Redding, Judge.



DISPOSITION: On appeal, reversed and remanded for resentencing; cross-appeal dismissed as abandoned.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision by the Multnomah County Circuit Court, Oregon, which refused to order defendant, who had been convicted of two counts of first degree robbery with a firearm, to serve a 30-year gun minimum sentence pursuant to former Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.610(4)(c) (2001) (amended 2005). Instead, the trial court imposed a 10-year gun minimum sentence. Defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1982, defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree robbery. In 1983, the trial court held an evidentiary hearing without a jury and found that defendant had used or threatened to use a firearm in the commission of the robbery. Defendant did not appeal or seek postconviction relief regarding his conviction or the gun minimum sentence imposed for that conviction. The instant court concluded that the legislature did not intend to allow a challenge to predicate convictions in subsequent sentence enhancement proceedings under former Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.610 (2001). The legislature intended defendants to have previously obtained relief on direct appeal or through postconviction relief from any prior unconstitutional sentences. Defendant's failure to resort to either of those remedies left his 1983 conviction and sentence in existence in the record as a legally cognizable judgment of a conviction and sentence for a felony having as an element the use or threatened use of a firearm. Consequently, the 1983 conviction and sentence, combined with a 1991 robbery conviction and sentence, subjected defendant to enhanced punishment under former Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.610(4)(c).


OUTCOME: On the State's appeal, the trial court's decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for resentencing. Defendant's cross-appeal was dismissed as abandoned.

State v. Robertson


A117093


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


207 Ore. App. 464; 142 P.3d 113; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1234


June 27, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
August 30, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Robertson, 342 Ore. 254, 149 P.3d 1213, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 1415 (2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Robertson v. Oregon, 127 S. Ct. 1886, 167 L. Ed. 2d 373, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3663 (U.S., 2007)
Review granted by, Vacated by, Remanded by State v. Robertson, 2008 Ore. LEXIS 865 (Or., Oct. 3, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 99C-56280. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Joseph C. Guimond, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Sentences vacated; remanded for resentencing; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court, Marion County, Oregon of robbery in the first degree with a firearm under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 164.415, 161.610; robbery in the second degree under Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.405; unlawful use of a weapon under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.220; and felon in possession of a firearm, Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.270.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pro se filed a notice of appeal the day before trial, seeking review of the denial of various pretrial rulings. The trial court concluded that Or. Rev. Stat. § 19.235 applied and that it retained jurisdiction to proceed to trial. The court dismissed that appeal. The court affirmed as to the conviction and found that Or. R. App. P. 7.15(3) was inapposite because the court's original order dismissing the first appeal was the product of sua sponte consideration, and that ruling pertained derivatively to the court's jurisdiction to address the substantive merits of that appeal. Any arguable constraint on the court's ability to revisit its determination that the pendency of the original appeal deprived the trial court of jurisdiction must derive from "law of the case." The court also held that Or. Rev. Stat. § 19.235 was intended to apply to both civil and criminal cases, and thus the trial court properly exercised its authority under § 19.235(1) and (2). However, under Ramirez, the trial court's imposition of the upward departure sentence was error apparent on the face of the record.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to the conviction. The court vacated the sentences and remanded for resentencing.

 

485 of 770 DOCUMENTS


In re Conner


A130828


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


207 Ore. App. 223; 140 P.3d 1167; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 1123


April 11, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
August 2, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 2005-819401. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Susan M. Svetkey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a Jehovah's Witness, appealed an order of the Multnomah County Circuit Court, Oregon, authorizing the administration of transfusions using whole blood products despite petitioner's religious beliefs and the wishes of his parents.


OVERVIEW: When petitioner was 17 years old, he learned that he had lymphoblastic leukemia. Petitioner sought to establish a common-law mature minor exception to the statute allowing a juvenile court judge to authorize emergency medical care. The instant court declined to decide the issue raised by petitioner because petitioner had turned 18 years old, rendering the juvenile court's order moot. Although petitioner argued the juvenile court continued to have jurisdiction pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 419.328, that statute did not apply to petitioner. The juvenile court derived its statutory authority to order medical care from Or. Rev. Stat. § 419B.110. Although the juvenile court may have lawfully issued an order that applied to petitioner, it did not do so pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 419B.100. That being the case, petitioner was never found to be within the juvenile court's jurisdiction as provided in Or. Rev. Stat. § 419B.100. Thus, Or. Rev. Stat § 419B.328(2)(e) did not authorize the juvenile court to exercise continuing jurisdiction over petitioner, who was no longer a child. The order authorizing emergency medical care ceased to have any legal effect on petitioner's 18th birthday.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed as moot.

Clarke v. Or. Health Scis. Univ.


A124560


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


206 Ore. App. 610; 138 P.3d 900; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 937


October 26, 2005, Argued and Submitted  
July 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Clarke v. Or. Health Sci. Univ., 341 Ore. 449, 143 P.3d 772, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 972 (2006)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Clarke v. Or. Health Scis. Univ., 2007 Ore. LEXIS 1233 (Or., Dec. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0005-05116. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Henry Kantor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions to reinstate judgment against OHSU in the amount of $ 200,000 and to reinstate claims against the individual defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, injured patient by his guardian ad litem, challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) that granted defendant hospital's motion to substitute itself as the sole defendant in place of defendants, other individual defendants, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(1), and limited the hospital's liability to the maximum award under the limits of the Oregon Tort Claims Act (OTCA), Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 30.260 to 30.300.


OVERVIEW: The patient's guardian filed a medical malpractice suit after the patient was deprived of oxygen while recuperating from successful surgery for a congenital heart defect. The hospital admitted its negligence, and the trial court resolved the case on the pleadings by limiting the judgment to the maximum amount under the OTCA and disposing of the claims against the individual defendants. On appeal, the patient claimed that the trial court deprived him of his rights to a remedy and to a jury trial under Or. Const. art. I, §§ 10 and 7. The court rejected the patient's claim that the OTCA damages cap deprived him of a remedy because although the hospital had been separated from the state education system, the hospital remained an instrumentality of the state and thus would have been immune from liability. Thus the OTCA did not deprive the patient of a remedy or his jury trial right. However, the court held that the patient would have had a common law remedy against the individual defendants and the application of Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(1) of the OTCA limiting the patient's remedy to the hospital, was not an adequate substitute remedy, and thus violated Or. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court judgment that disposed of the patient's claims against the individual defendants and affirmed the portion of the judgment that limited the hospital's liability to the damages cap in the OTCA. The court remanded the case with instructions to reinstate the judgment against the hospital in the amount of $ 200,000 and to reinstate the patient's claims against the individual defendants.

State v. Willingham


A126258


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


206 Ore. App. 156; 136 P.3d 66; 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 730


January 18, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
May 31, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0308-08747. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Michael C. Zusman, Judge pro tempore.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State challenged a decision from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment to defendant property owner in an action to recover medical assistance paid to the owner's father during his lifetime under Or. Rev. Stat. § 414.105.


OVERVIEW: In 1993, the father transferred property to the owner, his son, reserving a life estate. In 1997, the father applied for medical assistance from the State. After his death, the State filed a complaint against the owner to recover the amount paid under Or. Rev. Stat. § 414.105 and Or. Admin. R. 461-135-0845. The State argued that an amendment to Or. Rev. Stat. § 414.105 abrogated the common law rule that a life estate was extinguished at the moment of death for purposes of recovering medical assistance payments. The trial court granted summary judgment to the owner, and the State sought review. In reversing, the appellate court agreed that the life estate continued to exist under § 414.105, as amended. Moreover, this applied regardless of when the life estate was created. The appellate court also found that Or. Admin. R. 461-135-0845 also applied retroactively based upon its express language. Finally, the appellate court declined to address the owner's as applied constitutional challenges because they had not been considered by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.
