State v. Ross


A115701


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


199 Ore. App. 1; 110 P.3d 630; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 450


September 30, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
April 13, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by, On reconsideration by State v. Ross, 200 Ore. App. 143, 113 P.3d 921, 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 738 (2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Ross v. Franke, 254 Ore. App. 650, 297 P.3d 486, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 113 (2013)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Dismissed by Ross v. Taylor, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 135623 (D. Or., Sept. 30, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CM0021223. Appeal from Circuit Court, Benton County. Robert Gardner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Remanded for resentencing as to costs of court-appointed counsel; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court, Benton County (Oregon) of seven counts of rape in the first degree, one count of unlawful sexual penetration in the first degree, five counts of sodomy in the first degree, six counts of using a child in a sexually explicit display, and seven counts of sexual abuse in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 163.375, 163.411, 163.405, 163.670, 163.427. Defendant was sentenced and appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexually abusing his son, daughter, and stepdaughter. The court remanded for resentencing, but otherwise affirmed. Pursuant to Or. R. App. P. 5.45(1), defendant failed to preserve the issue of whether the State laid an adequate foundation for scientific evidence. The record demonstrated that the trial court complied with the requirements of Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.645 that it was to consider defendant's ability to pay a fine to the victims. The fines, which totalled over $ 22,000, were within the range of authority under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.101(1). The trial court erred in ordering defendant to pay court-appointed attorney fees because the trial court made no findings with respect to defendant's ability to pay as required by Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 161.665(3) (1999) and Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.675(1). The court rejected defendant's claim that the trial court erred in ordering unitary assessments under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.290 (1999) on the ground that it failed to consider his ability to pay under the statute. Section 137.290 did not impose an affirmative obligation on the trial court to make any particular findings as a predicate to imposing the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for resentencing as to the costs of court-appointed counsel. Otherwise, the court affirmed.

State v. Harberts


A114825


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


198 Ore. App. 546; 108 P.3d 1201; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 341


September 28, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
March 30, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Harberts, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 621 (Or., June 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CR0002110. Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. Robert D. Herndon, Judge.
State v. Harberts, 331 Ore. 72, 11 P.3d 641, 2000 Ore. LEXIS 697 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted, before the Circuit Court, Clackamas County, Oregon, of sexual abuse in the first degree, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.425 (former 1983), renumbered as Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.427 (1991). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's murder conviction in another case was reversed on appeal. In the present case, the victim was the daughter of the dead girl's father's girlfriend. At the time of the murder, the victim denied having been sexually abused by defendant. Years later, the victim alleged that defendant had sexually abused her some 11 to 13 years earlier. In the interim, the statute of limitations, Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.125(2)(k) (amended 1991), was amended to provide that a prosecution for first degree sexual abuse must be commenced before a victim attained the age of 24 or within six years after the offense was reported. Defendant advanced two arguments: (1) the application of the statute's latest version violated ex post facto prohibitions; and (2) the current statute of limitations had run. Nevertheless, the retroactive extension of an unexpired statute of limitations was not an impermissible alteration of the rules of evidence. Moreover, the indictment, which was issued only a month after the victim reported to law enforcement, was not time-barred. On a different issue, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to allow, based on relevancy, examination about the murder.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Sears v. Sears


A117631


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


198 Ore. App. 377; 108 P.3d 639; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 262


December 22, 2004, Submitted on Remand  
March 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Sears v. Sears, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 473 (Or., Aug. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On remand from the Oregon Supreme Court, Sears v. Sears, 337 Ore. 555, 101 P3d 809 (2004). Appeal from Circuit Court, Lincoln County. Robert J. Huckleberry, Judge. 01-2933.
Sears v. Sears, 190 Ore. App. 483, 79 P.3d 359, 2003 Ore. App. LEXIS 1550 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court had awarded custody of the child to respondent grandparents. On appeal, it was previously determined that the grandparents failed to rebut the statutory presumption, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.119 (2003) that appellant mother had acted in the child's best interests. The grandparents had appealed to the Oregon Supreme Court, which had remanded the matter for additional consideration.


OVERVIEW: The record revealed that the mother was 17 years old when the child was born. The grandparents' son, who was the child's father, was 15 years old. The mother left the child in the grandparents' care so that she could become the primary caretaker for the child's father. On remand, the appellate court remained satisfied that the grandparents had not shown, by a preponderance of the evidence, that the mother was unable or unwilling to provide adequate care for the child. In fact, the evidence showed that the relationship that developed between the mother and the child as a result of increasingly regular contacts had been positive and loving. The mother was an attentive and responsible parental figure. By leaving the child in the care of the grandparents, the mother acted in the child's best interests, not contrary to them, in encouraging and consenting to the relationship between grandparents and the child. The appellate court adhered to its original disposition of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court, once again, reversed the judgment. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

Mabon v. Wilson


A121483


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


198 Ore. App. 340; 108 P.3d 598; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 266


January 7, 2005, Submitted on Record and Briefs  
March 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Mabon v. Wilson, 338 Ore. 680, 115 P.3d 245, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 465 (2005)
Affirmed by Mabon v. Wilson, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 277 (Or., Apr. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Edward Jones, Judge. 0212-12568.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which dismissed an action filed under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.510 that challenged the authority of defendant judge to hold the office of circuit judge on the contention that defendant failed to subscribe to the correct oath of office.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff claimed that defendant did not subscribe and file the oath of office set forth in Or. Const. art. VII, § 21. The question was whether a private party could bring an action under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.510. The court held in reviewing prior enacted versions of the Oregon statutes, that nothing raised doubt that actions under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.619 had to be commenced and prosecuted by the district attorney. The statutes creating the action that substituted for the common-law quo warranto action expressly required such actions to be commenced and prosecuted by the district attorney, and because the district attorney neither commenced nor prosecuted the action, the trial court lacked jurisdiction over the case. Through a contextual analysis and a review of the prior enacted versions of the same statute, the review supported the conclusion that the statutory actions had to be commenced and prosecuted by the district attorney.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

529 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Porter


A120856


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


198 Ore. App. 274; 108 P.3d 107; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 238


November 9, 2004, Argued and submitted  
March 9, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Washington County. C022718CR. Nancy W. Campbell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Washington County, Oregon, convicted defendant of eight counts of identity theft and one count of unlawful use of a computer. The trial court disallowed defendant's demurrer to the indictment under the identity theft statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.800, and denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.800 violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8. The appellate court had to analyze the statute only to the extent that it purported to criminalize creating or uttering the identification of another with the intent to deceive. A person who either created or uttered the identification of another and who intended that act to deceive had taken a substantial step toward accomplishing the deception; the person had attempted to achieve the harm. The identity theft statute focused on the attempt to cause a forbidden harm, that is, deceit. As used by the legislature in the context of identity theft, the term "deceit" denoted an attempt to obtain some benefit to which the deceiver was not lawfully entitled. Thus narrowed, Or. Rev. Stat. § 165.800 did not reach a significant amount of privileged expression. Defendant's motion to suppress evidence was properly denied where officers had observed drug use and paraphernalia through the window and heard a person who, they reasonably believed, could be destroying the evidence. They were justified in conducting a "sweep" of the upstairs and in using information obtained thereby in their application for a warrant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

A120585


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9912-13689. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Jean K. Maurer, Judge.
Smurfit Newsprint Corp. v. Ass'n of W. Pulp & Paper Workers, Local 60, 2001 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25771 (D. Or., Aug. 14, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, modified in part, and reversed in part. Affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a class and sub-classes of employees, appealed a decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which found in their actions for untimely payment of wages, that defendant employer owed union plaintiffs penalties for failing to pay their regular wages on time but not for failing to pay severance benefits on time. The trial court also found that defendant did not owe salaried plaintiffs for unauthorized insurance deductions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs maintained that the sale of defendant's facility amounted to a termination of their employment and that defendant failed to pay them regular wages and severance benefits. The court held: (1) the transition between plaintiffs' employment with defendant and their employment with the new owner was a termination by defendant for purposes of Or. Rev. OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of plaintiffs on the claim for penalty wages was modified to begin the penalty period on November 11, 1999, and to include prejudgment interest. The court reversed the judgment against plaintiffs on the issue of unauthorized deductions of insurance premiums, and on their claim for penalty wages based on failure to timely pay severance. The court otherwise affirmed.

City of Lowell v. Wilson


A118815

DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon) that dismissed her appeal of a municipal court decision that convicted her of multiple violations of Lowell, Or., Ordinance No. 130, pertaining to owners of dangerous buildings. The City argued that the court lacked jurisdiction to hear the appeal under the three statutes that granted appellate jurisdiction, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 221.360, 138.050, and 138.057.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had argued that the municipal court lacked jurisdiction under the new city charter to hear the ordinance violations complaint and that the fine imposed exceeded the municipal court's authority. Defendant also argued for the first time on appeal that the sentenced imposed did not comport with due process, and thus was unconstitutional. The circuit court had dismissed defendant's appeal. On review, the court held that Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 138.050 and 138.57 were inapplicable because they did not apply to cases arising from convictions in municipal court for municipal code violations. Stat. § 221.360 as construed in City of Salem v. Polanski, which required a challenge to the constitutionality of an ordinance. The court held that it lacked jurisdiction under § 221.360 because defendant's constitutional challenge was not cognizable on appeal since it was never raised and preserved before the municipal court or the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal.

Hinton v. Hill


A121726


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


197 Ore. App. 238; 105 P.3d 923; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 88


October 5, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
February 2, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On reconsideration by, Clarified by, Adhered to Hinton v. Hill, 201 Ore. App. 131, 117 P.3d 1066, 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 1023 (2005)
Reversed by, Remanded by Hinton v. Hill, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 1397 (Or., Dec. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. 01C-10035. Jamese L. Rhoades, Judge.
State v. Hinton, 172 Ore. App. 483, 19 P.3d 390, 2001 Ore. App. LEXIS 194 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Judgment granting post-conviction relief vacated; remanded with instructions to vacate convictions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which granted post-conviction relief, arguing that the post-conviction court erred by failing to conclude that her convictions were void.


OVERVIEW: The post-conviction court found that petitioner was not informed of the potential incarceration beyond the 226 months stated in the plea petition. Petitioner asserted that she was denied adequate assistance of counsel under Or. Const. art. I, § 11. The court reversed, agreeing that the post-conviction court's findings and the judgment were internally inconsistent because petitioner sought relief under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.530(1)(a), and the court granted relief finding that petitioner was not informed of the maximum sentences to which her pleas expose her. That was not consistent with the determinations that petitioner knowingly and voluntarily made her pleas. Because the evidence supported the finding that petitioner was not informed of the maximum sentences, it followed that she was denied adequate assistance of counsel. The trial court sentenced her to a total incarcerative sentence in excess of the putative maximum sentence set out in the plea petition. Accordingly, petitioner was prejudiced by the constitutional violation. Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.530(1)(a) required the post-conviction court, in granting relief, to treat petitioner's convictions as void.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting post-conviction relief was vacated and the case was remanded with instructions to vacate convictions.

State v. Anderson


A121088


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


197 Ore. App. 193; 104 P.3d 1175; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 77


September 30, 2004 Argued and submitted.  
January 26, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Anderson, 338 Ore. 583, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 294 (Or., May 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 02-4169-DFE. Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. R. B. White, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In the Circuit Court of Jackson County, Oregon, defendant pled guilty to second-degree robbery, a so-called "Measure 11" crime, or one that carried a statutory minimum sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.700. Defendant appealed, asserting the trial court erred in ruling that she did not qualify for a lesser sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.712(2)(d), which provided a discretionary exception to a Measure 11 sentence for second-degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's plea to second-degree robbery was based on an aiding and abetting theory. Second-degree robbery was a Measure 11 offense with a mandatory minimum sentence of 70 months, which was what defendant received. However, under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.712(1)(a), the sentencing court could depart from the mandatory minimum sentence for second degree robbery if certain requirements under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.712(2)(d) were met. The trial court found defendant did not meet the criterion in Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.712(2)(d)(C), because her codefendant was armed with a "deadly weapon." However, the appellate court did not reach the merits of defendant's argument that the trial court erred as to the latter finding, because under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050(1), her sentence was not appealable. To be appealable after a plea of guilty or no contest under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050(1), a "disposition," (within the meaning of that term as defined in Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.053) had to either be unconstitutionally cruel and unusual, or exceed the maximum allowable by law. Defendant's sentence did not exceed the legal maximum and the appellate court did not have jurisdiction to review the matter.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Bray


02022413C; A120293


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


197 Ore. App. 12; 104 P.3d 631; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 5


September 29, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
January 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Bray, 340 Ore. 672, 136 P.3d 742, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 556 (2006)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Bray, 2007 Ore. LEXIS 501 (Or., June 1, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; sentences vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Malheur County Circuit Court, Oregon, which convicted him of four counts of encouraging child sexual abuse in the first degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.684, and 11 counts of encouraging child sexual abuse in the second degree, in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.686.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant raised numerous assignments of error. The instant court addressed only two of defendant's arguments: (1) whether the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on four charges of encouraging child sexual abuse in the first degree; and (2) whether the trial court erred in imposing upward departure sentences on a number of the convictions. The instant court rejected defendant's argument that the trial court should have granted his motion for judgment of acquittal, holding that the provision of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.684(1)(a)(A) concerning possession of child pornography with the intent to print that material did not require proof of defendant's intent to show or distribute the child pornography to another person. Thus, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the four charges of encouraging child sexual abuse in the first degree at issue on appeal. However, the trial court erred in imposing the departure sentences, which violated the Sixth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed, the sentences were vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Davis


A116035 (Control), A116439 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


197 Ore. App. 1; 104 P.3d 602; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 2



January 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Davis, 339 Ore. 230, 119 P.3d 790, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 538 (2005)
Appeal after remand at State v. Hamilton, 229 Ore. App. 94, 209 P.3d 851, 2009 Ore. App. LEXIS 747 (2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Davis v. Premo, 248 Ore. App. 262, 274 P.3d 896, 2012 Ore. App. LEXIS 190 (2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Davis v. Nooth, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 45375 (D. Or., Feb. 17, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 00-12-39969, 00-12-39970. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Kimberly C. Frankel, Judge. On appellant's petition for reconsideration filed August 18, 2004, and respondent's response to petition for reconsideration filed September 1, 2004. Opinion filed August 4, 2004. 194 Ore. App 382, 95 P3d 230.
State v. Davis, 194 Ore. App. 382, 95 P.3d 230, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 933 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reconsideration allowed; former opinion modified and adhered to as modified; defendant Davis's convictions and sentences affirmed; defendant Hamilton's convictions affirmed; defendant Hamilton's case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Multnomah County, Oregon, convicted defendant and co-defendant of multiple robbery convictions, and the matter was affirmed on appeal. Both parties petitioned in consolidated cases for reconsideration concerning the number of convictions that should have been entered, and defendant requested consideration a supplemental assignment of error concerning the imposition of an upward departure sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant held up a bar. Defendant shot at pursuing police officers and ultimately was convicted of attempted first-degree assault with a firearm, with an upward departure sentence of 72 months. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in rejecting his argument that the upward departure sentence was unconstitutional. The State suggested that the sentence imposed for a prior conviction was encompassed in the "fact" of the prior conviction, and because sentencing was not done by a jury in Oregon, consideration of facts pertaining to sentences for prior convictions did not intrude on any jury function. The appellate court ruled that the upward departure sentence was unconstitutional. The crucial fact at issue was whether defendant was on supervision at a particular point in time after that prior conviction had been entered. Even if the State were correct that the "fact" of the prior conviction included the sentence imposed for that conviction, it would not encompass facts concerning when defendant actually served either the prison term or the supervision term of that sentence.


OUTCOME: Reconsideration was allowed, the convictions were affirmed, co-defendant's sentences were affirmed, and defendant's case was remanded for resentencing.

Washburn v. Columbia Forest Prods.


A116664


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


197 Ore. App. 104; 104 P.3d 609; 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 17; 16 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 559; 11 Accom. Disabilities Dec. (CCH) 11-207


April 8, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
January 12, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Washburn v. Columbia Forest Prods., 339 Ore. 156, 119 P.3d 224, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 469 (2005)
Reversed by Washburn v. Columbia Forest Prods., 2006 Ore. LEXIS 354 (Or., May 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0012-12516. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Nely Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff millwright appealed a judgment of the Multnomah County Circuit Court, Oregon, which granted summary judgment to defendant former employer on the millwright's claim that the former employer had failed to meet its obligation to reasonably accommodate his disability under Oregon disability law.


OVERVIEW: The millwright, who used medical marijuana to help him sleep, challenged the trial court's conclusions that: (1) mitigating measures had to be considered when determining whether or not an individual was disabled and therefore protected by Oregon disability law; and (2) the Oregon Medical Marijuana Act, specifically Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.340(2), exempted employers from accommodating employees reporting to work with evidence of marijuana in their systems. The instant court concluded that the trial court incorrectly granted summary judgment insofar as it reasoned as a matter of law that the millwright was not a disabled person based on the fact that a mitigating measure--use of marijuana--alleviated his difficulty sleeping. The proper issue was whether the millwright's sleep, a major life activity, was substantially limited without mitigating measures. As to that issue, there was a genuine issue of a material fact. Because the millwright did not engage in the medical use of marijuana in the workplace, the trial court erred in concluding that § 475.340(2) excused the former employer from reasonably accommodating the millwright and granting summary judgment on that basis.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

540 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Illig-Renn


A114387


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


196 Ore. App. 765; 103 P.3d 1178; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1672


October 20, 2004, Submitted on Remand  
December 29, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Modified by, Adhered to, On reconsideration by State v. Illig-Renn, 199 Ore. App. 124, 110 P.3d 137, 2005 Ore. App. LEXIS 454 (Or. Ct. App., Apr. 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On remand from the Oregon Supreme Court, State v. Illig-Renn, 337 Ore. 327, 99 P.3d 290 (2004). Appeal from Circuit Court, Clackamas County. CR0014215. Eve L. Miller, Judge.
State v. Illig-Renn, 337 Ore. 327, 99 P.3d 290, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 599 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Reversal of an order granting defendant's demurrer to a charge of violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.247(1) as announced by the Circuit Court, Clackamas County (Oregon) was on remand from the Oregon Supreme Court for reconsideration in light of a newly announced rule regarding the constitutionality of disorderly conduct statutes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with disorderly conduct in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 162.247(1). Defendant demurred to the charge arguing that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court allowed the demurrer agreeing with defendant's argument. The trial court's decision was reversed on appeal, and the matter was taken to the Oregon Supreme Court. The supreme court remanded the matter in light of a recent decision regarding the constitutionality of a similar statutory provision. The court reconsidered the matter and noted that a statute was unconstitutionally overbroad if it prohibited a significant amount of constitutionally protected conduct or speech and it was not susceptible to a narrowing construction that would have conformed to legislative intent. The court concluded that the provisions of § 162.247(1) were constitutionally vague and violated the provisions of Or. Const. art. I, §§ 8 and 26, which protected free speech and the right to peaceably assemble. Accordingly, the statute was declared unconstitutional, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Stroup v. Hill


A119664


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


196 Ore. App. 565; 103 P.3d 1157; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1639


June 28, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
December 15, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Stroup v. Hill, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 189 (Or., Apr. 12, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CV01-1727. Appeal from Circuit Court, Umatilla County. Daniel J. Hill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Circuit Court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Umatilla County (Oregon), which found in favor of respondent superintendent and dismissed the inmate's petition for post-conviction relief, pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510 et seq.


OVERVIEW: The inmate brought a petition for post-conviction relief, alleging that his sentence for felon in possession of a firearm should have been vacated because it exceeded the statutory maximum sentence for a Class C felony, as provided by Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.605 and Or. Admin. R. 213-005-0002(4). The court affirmed the denial of the petition, stating that it disagreed that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to impose a sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.530(1)(b). Although Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.222(2)(d) precluded appellate review of the inmate's sentence, it did not follow therefrom that he was precluded from withdrawing his plea made pursuant to the agreement before sentencing in the trial court. He did not allege any other circumstances to show why he reasonably could not have been expected to raise his objection before sentencing. The court therefore concluded that, although he alleged a valid substantive ground for post-conviction relief, he did not satisfy the procedural requirement of Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.550(2). He also did not demonstrate that any inadequacy of his trial counsel led to a different result in the proceeding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gornick


A121042


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


196 Ore. App. 397; 102 P.3d 734; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1611


September 21, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
December 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Gornick, 338 Ore. 583, 114 P.3d 504, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 278 (2005)
Reversed by State v. Gornick, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 172 (Or., Mar. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. 02C53376. Susan Tripp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence vacated; remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Marion County (Oregon), which convicted him, upon his guilty plea, of assault in the third degree, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.165, and found several aggravating factors that it deemed to be substantial and compelling reasons to impose an upward durational departure sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for third-degree assault after spitting at a staff member at a youth correctional facility, where defendant was incarcerated. He pled guilty. Defendant's presumptive sentence under the sentencing guidelines was 13 to 14 months. The trial court determined that defendant's case was appropriate for departure from the sentencing guidelines based on evidence that defendant had been resistive to treatment and sanctioned on other occasions, and that the spitting incident included throwing a chair through a window and breaking it along with "lots of inappropriate statements and behavior." The trial court sentenced defendant to 26 months, followed by two years of post-prison supervision. On appeal, the court found that the trial court committed plain error in imposing the sentence, finding that the waiver of defendant's Sixth Amendment right to a jury trial implicit in the guilty plea did not include a waiver of the right to have a jury determine aggravating factors that would support a departure. The court found that there was no basis in the record for the inference that defendant intentionally waived the right to jury determination of the aggravating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded the cause for resentencing.

Simonsen v. Ford Motor Co.


A119931


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


196 Ore. App. 460; 102 P.3d 710; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1615; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,234


June 10, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
December 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Simonsen v. Ford Motor Co., 2005 Ore. LEXIS 375 (Or., July 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. 01 C19139. Joseph V. Ochoa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of dismissal with respect to specification "C" of plaintiff's claim for negligence reversed and remanded; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which found in favor of defendant manufacturer and dismissed the driver's claims after she was severely injured in an accident while driving a car manufactured by the manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: The driver, who was severely injured in an accident while driving a car manufactured by the manufacturer, appealed from a judgment dismissing her claims against the manufacturer pursuant to Or. R. Civ. P. 21(A)(9). The trial court determined that her claims were barred by the statute of ultimate repose for product liability civil actions, former Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905(1) (2001), and the statute of limitations for breach of warranty claims, Or. Rev. Stat. § 72.7250(1). The court affirmed the trial court's disposition with respect to two of the driver's three specifications of negligence and her warranty claims. However, her remaining specification of negligence alleged conduct that was not subject to former Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.905(1) (2001) and, from the pleadings, the court could not determine whether that specification was barred by the applicable statutes of limitations and ultimate repose, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 12.110 and 12.115. Because specification "C" did not disclose the date of the "act or omission complained of," the pleadings did not show that the allegation was barred under § 12.115. Consequently, the court erred in dismissing specification "C."


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the dismissal with respect to certain specifications of the driver's claim for negligence. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

Walton v. Thompson


A112207


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


196 Ore. App. 335; 102 P.3d 687; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1549


March 10, 2004, Submitted on Record and Briefs  
December 1, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Walton v. Thompson, 338 Ore. 375, 110 P.3d 114, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 157 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 97C10421; Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Jamese Rhoades, Judge.
State v. Walton, 134 Ore. App. 66, 894 P.2d 1212, 1995 Ore. App. LEXIS 657 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Marion County, Oregon, which denied his petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the trial court erred in rejecting his claim that his consecutive sentences on two counts of aggravated murder were unlawful. The instant court concluded that petitioner's challenge could reasonably have been raised on direct appeal. It was significant, albeit not dispositive, that petitioner's criminal trial counsel raised and preserved an objection to the imposition of the multiple sentences for aggravated murder. At the time counsel raised the objection, there was no authoritative decision by the Oregon Supreme Court. It would not have been unreasonable for appellate counsel to have raised the already preserved issue before the instant court in order to seek review by the Supreme Court of a novel issue of statutory construction. Nothing in this record suggested that appellate counsel's failure in that regard was excused by anything even approaching futility. Petitioner failed to establish that his challenge could not reasonably have been asserted on direct appeal. Accordingly, the trial court properly denied post-conviction relief on that ground.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Washington County, Oregon, imposed consecutive sentences on defendant for his convictions of robbery in the first degree, robbery in the second degree, kidnapping in the first degree, assault in the second degree, and unauthorized use of a vehicle, all of which arose out of a carjacking episode. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in imposing mandatory sentences for certain crimes pursuant to Or. Rev. Morsman v. City of Madras


A125106


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


196 Ore. App. 67; 100 P.3d 761; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1416


August 6, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
November 3, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Morsman v. City of Madras, 338 Ore. 374, 110 P.3d 113, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 153 (2005)
Appeal after remand at Morsman v. City of Madras, 2006 Ore. App. LEXIS 8 (Or. Ct. App., Jan. 4, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 2003-170. Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals.
Morsman v. City of Madras, 191 Ore. App. 149, 81 P.3d 711, 2003 Ore. App. LEXIS 1718 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent City annexed certain real property, petitioner land owners brought suit challenging the constitutionality of the "triple majority" method of annexation the City employed pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 222.170. The Oregon Land Use Board of Appeals concluded, inter alia, that the owners waived their constitutional objections to the triple-majority method of annexation. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The instant appeal was the third time the underlying dispute had been brought before the courts. On review, the owners challenged the board's waiver determination and asserted that the consents obtained by the City were invalid, as they were obtained before the City reconfigured the area to be annexed. The appellate court found that the board's analysis did not account for one of the land owners who was not a party to the first prior case in the underlying dispute; nor could that owner's failure to participate in the first prior suit be itself deemed a waiver, as the board explicitly acknowledged in the first prior suit that the City failed to comply with the notice requirements of Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.763(1). For similar reasons, the remaining land owners did not waive their constitutional challenge. However, the appellate court also held that the consents obtained by the City were not invalid, as Or. Rev. Stat. § 222.170 did not require consents to be reexecuted when the City altered the description of the areas to be annexed before it finally proclaimed the annexation.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment concluding that the land owners waived their constitutional objections to the triple-majority method of annexation was reversed and remanded to the board for reconsideration of the land owners' constitutional arguments; otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Atwood


A117917


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


195 Ore. App. 490; 98 P.3d 751; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1262


May 11, 2004, Argued and Submitted; Eastern Oregon University, La Grande  
October 6, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 010097CR. Appeal from Circuit Court, Lake County. Lane W. Simpson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction for disorderly conduct under ORS 166.025(1)(a) reversed; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of disorderly conduct: the first alleged that he engaged in tumultuous and threatening behavior in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(a), and the second count alleged that he made unreasonable noise in violation of Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(b). The Circuit Court of Lake County, Oregon, convicted defendant on both counts and denied his motions for judgment of acquittal. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the evidence was insufficient to convict him on each count of disorderly conduct. As to the first count, the appellate court found there was no physical impact at all; defendant merely gestured angrily. That did not constitute "the use of physical force." Thus, the evidence was insufficient to support a finding that defendant engaged in physical conduct that was immediately likely to produce the use of physical force by defendant. As such, the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal on the disorderly conduct count under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(a). However, denial for judgment of acquittal on the disorderly conduct count under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(b) was proper as the question of defendant's intent, whether his parting outburst was intended to be communicative or was merely a guise to disturb, was a quintessential jury question.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of disorderly conduct for engaging in tumultuous and threatening behavior was reversed. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

State v. Sawatzky


A116857 (Control), A117424 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


195 Ore. App. 159; 96 P.3d 1288; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1143


September 17, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
September 8, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition granted by State v. Sawatzky, 338 Ore. 585, 114 P.3d 505, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 286 (2005)
Writ dismissed by State v. Sawatzky, 339 Ore. 689, 125 P.3d 722, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 812 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0003-32189, 0009-37299. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. David Gernant, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Sentences vacated; cases remanded for resentencing; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant embezzled half a million dollars over several years in the course of her employment as a bookkeeper for her elderly employers. The Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon) imposed upward departure sentences in two cases that were consolidated for appeal. Defendant appealed the sentences, some of which were concurrent and some of which were consecutive, that added up to a total period of incarceration of 88 months.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant made three principal arguments: the trial court erred in relying on "abuse of trust" as a sentencing factor to support certain departure sentences; with respect to both cases, under Apprendi, the trial court could not impose upward departure sentences because the enhancement factors on which it relied were not based on the facts to which defendant pled guilty; again with respect to both cases, under the reasoning of State v. Quinn, reliance on certain upward departure factors pursuant to the sentencing guidelines violated Or. Const. art. I, § 11. The appellate court concluded that, under Blakely, the imposition of upward departure sentences in each of the consolidated cases was erroneous. It concluded that, consistently with Blakely, the relevant "prescribed statutory maximum" under the Oregon sentencing guidelines was the presumptive sentence that the court determined based on the offender's criminal history and crime seriousness score. Guidelines departure sentences, which required judicial findings of fact and were not, under the current scheme, based on facts found by the jury, did not comport with the Sixth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The sentences were vacated, the cases were remanded for resentencing, and the judgment was otherwise affirmed.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] FDA-02-2; Judicial Review from Fair Dismissal Appeals Board.
Bergerson v. Salem-Keizer Sch. Dist., 185 Ore. App. 649, 60 P.3d 1126, 2003 Ore. App. LEXIS 30 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded on petition; affirmed on cross-petition.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner district court review of the decision of the Fair Dismissal Appeals Board (FDAB) (Oregon), which found in favor of respondent teacher and ordered the district to reinstate the teacher to her former position. The teacher also cross-petitioned the decision.


OVERVIEW: The district was ordered to reinstate the former third-grade teacher after the district dismissed her on ground of "neglect of duty" and "immorality" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 342.865(1)(b) and (d) following an incident in which she drove her vehicle into the back of her estranged husband's pickup truck. He cross-petitioned, raising challenges to the various aspects of the order. The court reversed and remanded, finding in favor of the district and concluding that the FDAB did not adequately explain its reasoning with respect to the conclusion that the teacher's dismissal was unreasonable. In light of those facts, the FDAB failed to sufficiently explain why it determined that the school board's decision to dismiss the teacher was clearly an excessive remedy. Contrary to the teacher's assertions, the FDAB did not rely solely on the fact that she had attempted suicide in reaching the conclusion that her conduct constituted immorality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an remanded on the petition but affirmed the cross-petition.

Roop v. Parker Northwest Paving Co.


A104616 (Control), A104635, A104871 (Cases Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


194 Ore. App. 219; 94 P.3d 885; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 877


November 3, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
July 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Roop v. Parker Northwest Paving Co., 2005 Ore. LEXIS 152 (Or., Apr. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9709-06913, 9708-06502. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Anna Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on appeal and on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a paving company and its lawyer, voluntarily dismissed a defamation suit against plaintiffs, the hosts and guests of a cable show. Plaintiffs then sued for wrongful initiation of civil proceedings. The Circuit Court, Multnomah County, Oregon, struck claims for punitive damage, granted a directed verdict to the lawyer, and declined various jury instructions. A jury found for one guest and otherwise for the company. Both sides appealed.


OVERVIEW: The guests were members of a citizens' group that opposed the business's application to expand a gravel mining operation on a river. The reviewing court affirmed the decisions below, finding that: (1) as to the dismissal of the claim for punitive damages, even if the claim constituted a historical exception to the protections of Or. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Williams v. Philip Morris, Inc.


A106791


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 527; 92 P.3d 126; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 677; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P17,042


November 17, 2003, Submitted on Remand  
June 9, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Williams v. Philip Morris, Inc., 337 Ore. 669, 104 P.3d 601, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 872 (2004)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Williams v. Philip Morris, Inc., 340 Ore. 35, 127 P.3d 1165, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 31 (Or., Feb. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9705-03957. On remand from the United States Supreme Court, Philip Morris USA, Inc. v. Williams,     US    , 540 U.S. 801, 124 S Ct 56, 157 L Ed 2d 12 (2003). Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Anna J. Brown.
Philip Morris USA Inc. v. Williams, 540 U.S. 801, 124 S. Ct. 56, 157 L. Ed. 2d 12, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5437 (2003)
Williams v. Philip Morris Inc., 183 Ore. App. 192, 51 P.3d 670, 2002 Ore. App. LEXIS 1214 (2002)



DISPOSITION: On appeal, reversed and remanded with instructions to enter judgment on jury verdict; affirmed on cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This tobacco litigation was remanded from the United States Supreme Court for reconsideration of the jury's award of $ 79.5 million in punitive damages on a fraud claim brought by plaintiff, the estate of a deceased smoker, against defendant tobacco manufacturer.


OVERVIEW: From the early 1950s until his death from a smoking-related lung cancer in 1997, the decedent smoked the manufacturer's cigarettes. His estate sued the manufacturer for making intentionally false representations about the health effects of cigarette smoking. In addition to compensatory damages, the jury awarded the estate punitive damages of $ 79.5 million for fraud, which the trial court reduced to $ 32 million. The Court of Appeals of Oregon reinstated the jury verdict. On remand, the Court of Appeals was required to determine whether that award of punitive damages was consistent with the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment in light of recent United States Supreme Court precedent. The Court of Appeals held that the award of $ 79.5 million in punitive damages did not violate the Due Process Clause, because the amount of the award was reasonable and proportionate to the wrong inflicted on the decedent and the public.


OUTCOME: The award of punitive damages as originally found by the jury was reinstated.


 

552 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stubbs


A120041


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 595; 91 P.3d 774; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 688



June 9, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Stubbs, 195 Ore. App. 762, 100 P.3d 218, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 1346 (2004)
Review denied by State v. Stubbs, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 900 (Or., Dec. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 20-00-11795. Appeal from Circuit Court, Lane County. Lyle C. Velure, Judge. On respondent's motion to determine appellate jurisdiction filed February 2, 2004, and on appellant's motion to dismiss respondent's motion to determine appellate jurisdiction filed February 17, 2004.



DISPOSITION: Motion to determine jurisdiction allowed; appeal may proceed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an amended judgment of the Circuit Court, Lane County (Oregon), which altered his sentence on his convictions for criminally negligent homicide, felony failure to perform the duties of a driver, and tampering with physical evidence. The convictions were entered upon defendant's plea of guilty. The State filed a motion to determine whether the court had jurisdiction over the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The gravamen of defendant's argument on appeal was that the amended sentence imposed was not imposed consistently with statutory requirements, because the trial court lacked authority to modify a sentence that had already been executed, in light of Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.010(6). The court found that Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050 contained provisions limiting both appealability and reviewability and that the proper disposition of an appeal in which an appellant failed to make the colorable showing required by § 138.050(1) was dismissal. To be appealable after a plea of guilty or no contest under § 138.050(1), a "disposition," within the meaning of that term as defined in Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.053, had to either be unconstitutionally cruel and unusual or exceed the maximum allowable by law because it was not imposed consistently with statutory requirements. The court found that defendant's challenge concerned a "disposition," which by definition included imposition of a sentence pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.053(1)(a). Thus, defendant's argument was one that was cognizable as pertaining to a "disposition" that exceeded the maximum allowable by law under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.050(1)(a).


OUTCOME: The court allowed the motion to determine jurisdiction and ruled that the appeal could proceed.

Hood River Valley Residents' Comm., Inc. v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


A118889


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 485; 91 P.3d 748; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 639


November 25, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
June 2, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 020029CC. Appeal from Circuit Court, Hood River County. Donald H. Hull, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.040(1), petitioners, a nonprofit organization and an individual county resident, brought a petition for a writ of review challenging a decision by respondent Board of County Commissioners of Hood River County (county) to enter into a land exchange agreement with respondent limited partnership. The Circuit Court, Hood River County (Oregon), dismissed the petition. Petitioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the petition based on its determination that the challenged decision was not "quasi-judicial." Petitioners alleged that the county's decision did not comport with several statutes pertaining to exchanges of county lands, including Or. Rev. Stat. § 273.335, and, consequently, the county failed to follow the procedure applicable to the matter. The court reversed the dismissal, concluding that the land exchange decision was "quasi-judicial" for purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 34.040. The court stated that Or. Rev. Stat. § 275.335 required the county to apply preexisting criteria concerning value to concrete facts concerning the particular proposed land exchange and also prescribed certain procedural requirements for making that determination. Additionally, the court concluded that the resident had standing to pursue a writ of review. The resident specifically alleged how the development of a resort would likely affect his farming operation. Finally, the court denied the partnership's renewed motion to dismiss the appeal, stating that the motion was predicated upon consideration of evidentiary materials that had been proffered for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of dismissal and remanded the case. The court further denied the partnership's renewed motion to dismiss the appeal.

Kerr v. Bradbury


A121744


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 304; 89 P.3d 1227; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 567


February 11, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
May 5, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at Kerr v. Bradbury, 194 Ore. App. 133, 93 P.3d 841, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 837 (2004)
Review dismissed by Kerr v. Bradbury, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 221 (Or., Mar. 23, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 02C-21814. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Don A. Dickey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, three Oregon voters (voters), sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, the Secretary of State for the State of Oregon (secretary), in the voters' action for declaratory and injunctive relief arguing that an initiative petition could not be certified.


OVERVIEW: The secretary certified an initiative petition for circulation, even though the text of the petition set out only the wording proposed to be added to existing statutes and did not include the text of the statutes to be amended. The voters initiated an action for declaratory and injunctive relief, arguing that the initiative petition could be certified because it failed to include the text of the statutes as they would read if the proposed amendments were to be approved by the voters. The voters argued that the full text of the "proposed law" within the meaning of Or. Const. art. IV, § 1(2)(d) referred to the full text of the law as amended. On appeal the court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of the secretary and remanded for an entry of summary judgment in favor of the voters. The court stated that it seemed likely that, in adopting art. IV, § 1(2)(d), the voters intended to require publication of the full text of the statute as it would appear if amended, regardless of whether the amendment was proposed by the legislature of by initiative. Thus, the grant of summary judgment in favor of the secretary was improper.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for an entry of summary judgment in favor of the voters.

Bobo v. Kitzhaber


A120098


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 214; 89 P.3d 1189; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 542


August 19, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
April 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at Bobo v. Kitzhaber, 194 Ore. App. 419, 95 P.3d 731, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 932 (2004)
Review granted by Bobo v. Kitzhaber, 337 Ore. 282, 96 P.3d 347, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 527 (2004)
Reversed by Bobo v. Kulongoski, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 102 (Or., Feb. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 01C-15710. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Dennis J. Graves, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of an order from the Circuit Court, Marion County (Oregon), which denied their motion for summary judgment and awarded summary judgment to defendant State of Oregon in an action alleging that the State incorrectly determined the amount of money available for "kicker" tax refunds to taxpayers for the 1999-2001 biennium.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers brought an action against the State, alleging that it incorrectly determined the amount of money available for "kicker" tax refunds to taxpayers for the 1999-2001 biennium, reducing the "kicker" tax refund by about one-third. Both parties moved for summary judgment. The trial court granted the State's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that Medicaid Upper Payment Limit funds (MUPL funds) were received from Oregon General Fund revenue sources during the biennium and, consequently, had to be included in the "kicker" calculation. The MUPL funds were revenues received from General Fund revenue sources for purposes of Or. Rev. Stat. § 291.349(4). Regardless of the Oregon Legislature's later disposition of the funds, they were received from General Fund revenue sources when they were properly placed in the General Fund pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 293.110 in the first instance. That the Oregon Legislature redirected the funds elsewhere before the end of the biennium did not alter the practical and statutory reality that the revenues were received from a General Fund revenue source.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Am. Trucking Ass'ns v. State


A117694


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 185; 90 P.3d 15; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 539


October 15, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
April 28, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Am. Trucking Ass'ns v. State, 337 Ore. 669, 104 P.3d 601, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 869 (2004)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Am. Trucking Ass'ns v. DOT, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 726 (Or., Dec. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 00C-16242. Appeal from Circuit Court, Marion County. Claudia M. Burton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; remanded with instructions to enter declaratory judgment declaring the flat fee options unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trucking companies brought a declaratory action seeking an injunction and a refund of taxes paid against defendants, the State and the department of transportation et al, asserting that aspects of the manner in which the State taxed heavy trucks that used its highways violated the dormant Commerce Clause. The Circuit Court of Marion County, Oregon, ruled in the State's favor and dismissed the action. The companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the companies contended the statutory exceptions to the weight-mile system for taxing heavy trucks (the flat fee options under Or. Rev. Stat. § 825.480 and the fuel tax exception for farm vehicles under Or. Rev. Stat. § 805.310) violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8; they argued that the exceptions placed interstate commerce at a disadvantage when it competed with intrastate commerce. The appellate court found that the flat fee options discriminated between interstate and intrastate carriers whose businesses differed only because of their relationship to state boundaries, and the discrimination operated to the detriment of the interstate carrier. The flat fee options did not apportion the tax burden among the states where the interstate carrier operated, and they therefore failed the "internal consistency" test. However, the appellate court also found that the companies failed to show that the fuel tax discriminated between interstate and intrastate carriers; if every state adopted the fuel tax exception, there would not be any malapportionment or discrimination between interstate and intrastate carriers.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the flat fee options and remanded with instructions to enter declaratory judgment declaring the flat fee options unconstitutional and to award any appropriate relief; otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

Just v. City of Lebanon


2003-044; A122517


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


193 Ore. App. 132; 88 P.3d 312; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 468


November 3, 2003, Argued  
April 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Just v. City of Lebanon, 337 Ore. 247, 95 P.3d 728, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 489 (2004)
Review dismissed by Just v. City of Lebanon, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 1285 (Or., Dec. 5, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals.
Friends of Linn County v. City of Lebanon, 193 Ore. App. 151, 88 P.3d 322, 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 464 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on petitions; cross-petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a city and a family trust, challenged a decision of the Land Use Board of Appeals (LUBA) (Oregon), which ruled in favor of respondent citizen and remanded the city's annexation and zoning designation of approximately 61 acres of land abutting the city limits. The citizen filed a cross-petition for judicial review, which the city and trust moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The city sought to annex certain property and applied particular zoning designations to that property. The citizen appealed certain of those annexation and zoning decisions to LUBA. LUBA remanded the annexation and zoning designation because it found that the city failed to meet certain annexation criteria in its comprehensive plan. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the justiciability requirements articulated in case law did not apply to proceedings before LUBA because it was not a court in which the constitution vested judicial power. Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.805 did not require LUBA to apply the justiciability doctrine in the manner that the court had applied it in case law. Because the citizen appeared before the local government and filed a notice of intent to appeal, he had standing to appeal to LUBA under Or. Rev. Stat. § 197.830(2). Accordingly, LUBA did not err in refusing to dismiss the citizen's appeal on the ground that he lacked standing under case law. The citizen, as a respondent on review, did not need to establish that a decision would have had a practical effect on him. However, he lacked standing to pursue his cross-motion, which the court dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and dismissed the cross-petition.

Corp. of the Presiding Bishop v. City of W. Linn


A122194


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


192 Ore. App. 567; 86 P.3d 1140; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 316


October 6, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
March 24, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Corp. of the Presiding Bishop v. City of W. Linn, 337 Ore. 282, 96 P.3d 347, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 526 (2004)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Corp. of the Presiding Bishop v. City of W. Linn, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 204 (Or., May 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 2002-155. Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city denied respondent church's application for a conditional use permit to build a church meetinghouse in a residential neighborhood. The church appealed to the Oregon Land Use Board of Appeals, which determined that the city's decision violated certain provisions of the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act of 2000 (RLUIPA), 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 2000cc to 2000cc-5. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the city contended the board erred in determining that the RLUIPA was applicable to its decision and that its decision violated the RLUIPA. The appellate court found that, by its terms, the RLUIPA did not provide that religious entities were entirely exempt from land use regulations. Rather, the RLUIPA provided standards for the imposition of land use regulations on religious entities. Because the board did not interpret or apply the RLUIPA in a manner entirely exempting the church from land use regulations, the board's order remanding the case to the city for further determination was not erroneous. The city did not entirely prevent the church from building any church at all in the desired location. Rather, the burden imposed on the church was the burden of being prevented from implementing the particular design proposal at issue. The city's ordinances, as applied in the city's decision, did not impose a substantial burden on the church's religious exercise. Thus, the city's decision did not violate the RLUIPA and the board erred in concluding otherwise.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to affirm the city's denial of the church's application.

State v. O'Donnell


A113249


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


192 Ore. App. 234; 85 P.3d 323; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 200


October 31, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
February 25, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 9808-36958. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. David Gernant, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which found in favor of defendant, and dismissed with prejudice three counts of a criminal indictment against him.


OVERVIEW: The State appealed from an order dismissing with prejudice, and thus barring retrial of, three counts of a criminal indictment against defendant on which the jury failed to reach a verdict following a full trial. The trial court determined that retrial as to all three counts was barred by the statutory double jeopardy provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. § 131.515 and that, even if § 131.515 did not preclude retrial as to all three charges, retrial of the felony murder charge against defendant was precluded by constitutional double jeopardy protections. The court disagreed, reversed, and remanded for retrial of the three dismissed counts. The trial court's erroneous dismissal of the indictment did not operate to bar retrial where the prior trial was, in fact, properly terminated based on the jury's inability to reach a verdict. In that regard, defendant was in precisely the same position as he would have been if the trial court had never erroneously dismissed the indictment under § 131.515. He was subject to retrial because the jury was unable to reach a verdict and U.S. Const. amend. V demanded nothing more.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for the retrial of defendant's three dismissed counts.

W. Coast Media, LLC v. City of Gladstone


A121694


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


192 Ore. App. 102; 84 P.3d 213; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 110


July 17, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
February 11, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 2002-098. Judicial Review from Land Use Board of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought review of a decision by the Oregon Land Use Board of Appeals (LUBA) that reversed its denial of respondent media company's application to place outdoor advertising signs (billboards) on city land adjacent to the interstate.


OVERVIEW: The company had applied to the city to construct four billboards on property zoned for commercial and industrial uses. The proposed billboards were each 14 by 48 feet, or a total of 672 square feet per billboard. The city's building official denied the request based on advice from the city attorney that billboards were not a permitted land use within the city limits. LUBA reversed the city's denial of the application. LUBA concluded that the city's denial violated Or. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 20. The appellate court affirmed LUBA's reversal, but also held that the reversal did not mean that the city had to approve the company's application. The appellate court agreed that the city's municipal code did not permit all signs except for those specifically prohibited. It also agreed with LUBA that the city's denial violated Or. Const. art. I, § 8, as it was impossible to apply Gladstone, Or. Mun. Code § 17.52 without inquiry into the content of the proposed sign to determine if it was permitted. Thus, the city failed to apply any content-neutral distinction that would permit it to deny the company's application.


OUTCOME: The decision of the board was affirmed.

Wurtele v. Blevins


A115793


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


192 Ore. App. 131; 84 P.3d 225; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 112


October 3, 2003, Submitted on Record and Briefs  
February 11, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wurtele v. Blevins, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 752 (Or., Oct. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 00-3066. Appeal from Circuit Court, Columbia County. Steven Reed, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, Columbia County (Oregon), which awarded custody of his daughter to respondents, the child's maternal grandparents.


OVERVIEW: When the child was two-and-one-half years old, she began living with the grandparents, who acted in a parental role and provided care, nurturing, and security for the child. The mother maintained a continuing presence in the child's life, although living separately from the grandparents. Although the father maintained consistent contact with the child, his financial contributions toward her support were sporadic. The court held that the grandparents, by reference to Or. Rev. Stat. § 109.119(4)(b), had rebutted the statutory presumption that the father acted in the child's best interest. The grandparents had acted as the child's primary caretakers for five years, and no other relationship in the child's life qualitatively approached this primary bond. While the father's relationship was warm and affectionate, he never visited her school, talked with her teachers, checked with her doctors, or assumed any traditional parental role. The father's determination to preclude contact with the grandparents would, if realized, be detrimental to the child. The award of custody to the grandparents was in the child's best interests. Constitutionally sufficient compelling circumstances existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of custody to the grandparents.

State v. Hughes (In re Hughes)


A114527


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


192 Ore. App. 8; 83 P.3d 951; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 105


June 23, 2003, Submitted on Record and Briefs; November 5, 2003, Resubmitted En Banc  
February 4, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Hughes, 337 Ore. 282, 96 P.3d 347, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 523 (2004)
Review dismissed by State v. Hughes, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 60 (Or., Jan. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. 010362845. Lewis B. Lawrence, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an involuntarily committed mental patient, sought reversal of an order from the Circuit Court, Multnomah County (Oregon), which committed him for treatment under Or. Rev. Stat. § 426.005(1)(d)(A), (B) based upon findings that he was a danger to himself and unable to provide for his basic personal needs.


OVERVIEW: The patient's mother and sister reported that the patient was not taking his medications, was hallucinating, was not eating properly, and could not keep his house clean. At the civil commitment hearing, the patient behaved in an agitated manner and stated that he wanted to subpoena his sons to testify. The trial court, after stating that there was a substantial likelihood that the sons' evidence would not be helpful, found that the patient was unable to care for himself. The patient's counsel did not object to the statement that the sons' evidence would not be helpful. The court concluded that the trial court did not deny the patient an opportunity to subpoena witnesses. Under Or. R. Civ. P. 55(C)(1)(a)(ii), counsel could have issued a subpoena without the trial court's involvement. The trial court's statement amounted to an evidentiary ruling that, even if subpoenaed, the sons would not be permitted to testify. Because no offer of proof was made as to the content of expected testimony, the issue was not reviewable. The court noted that any error was harmless because the testimony and the patient's agitated behavior at the hearing sufficiently supported the commitment order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commitment order.

Perrin v. Kitzhaber

COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


191 Ore. App. 439; 83 P.3d 368; 2004 Ore. App. LEXIS 36


November 10, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
January 21, 2004, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Perrin v. Kitzhaber, 337 Ore. 247, 95 P.3d 728, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 488 (2004)
Review dismissed by Perrin v. Kitzhaber, 338 Ore. 17, 107 P.3d 27, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 61 (2005)
Review denied by Perrin v. Kitzhaber, 2005 Ore. LEXIS 260 (Or., May 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 0107-07021, 0107-07020. Appeal from Circuit Court, Multnomah County. Jean Kerr Maurer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Circuit court judgment reversed; case remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Multnomah County, Oregon, entered a judgment that: (1) declared congressional districts were unconstitutional; (2) enjoined defendant political officials from conducting future elections based on those districts; and (3) adopted a redistricting plan. The trial court denied plaintiff voters' and plaintiff political parties' request for attorney fees, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The voters and political parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: A census showed a shift in population, requiring redistricting of congressional districts. A plan was passed by the legislature, but the governor vetoed the plan, and there was no override. Two groups of voters, representing the interests of each political party, filed actions alleging claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. In its refusal to grant attorney fees, the trial court determined that no party was successful. The voters asserted that the trial court erred in its determination that they had not prevailed and in its application of the special circumstances exception in 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The appellate court determined the voters prevailed in this action, even though they failed to obtain the exact relief that they had sought. As to whether the special circumstances exception applied, the appellate court disagreed with the trial court's analysis. First, that the voters interests were partisan was immaterial. Furthermore, the defendants, were not just innocent bystanders in a turf war. The realities of the situation rendered the special circumstances exception inapposite.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment, and the matter was remanded to the trial court to determined the reasonableness of the fees requested.

Allen v. County of Jackson County


A115689


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


191 Ore. App. 185; 82 P.3d 628; 2003 Ore. App. LEXIS 1725


July 7, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
December 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Allen v. County of Jackson County, 337 Ore. 84, 93 P.3d 72, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 402 (2004)
Affirmed by Allen v. County of Jackson County, 2006 Ore. LEXIS 148 (Or., Feb. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 97-009-L1. Appeal from Circuit Court, Jackson County. Roxanne Osborne, Judge.
Allen v. County of Jackson, 169 Ore. App. 116, 7 P.3d 739, 2000 Ore. App. LEXIS 1164 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees sued defendant county for breach of contract and wrongful deduction from wages, seeking to recover retirement contributions that were deducted under an unconstitutional law. The appeals court held that plaintiffs stated a wage claim. On remand, the Circuit Court, Jackson County, Oregon, denied the employees' motions for judgment on the pleadings and for a directed verdict on the wage claim. The employees appealed.


OVERVIEW: Ballot Measure 8 required public employees to contribute six percent of their compensation to retirement accounts. It also prohibited employers from paying the contributions. Following its enactment, the county adopted an ordinance eliminating its payment of contributions but giving employees a 5.7 percent pay increase. The state supreme court later declared Measure 8 unconstitutional. The employees asserted that defendant violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 652.610(3) when it deducted six percent from their wages for retirement contributions while Measure 8 was in force. The jury found that the employees were entitled to damages for breach of contract in the amount of .3 percent of their total wages, and the trial court applied the same measure of damages to the wage claim. In affirming, the court reasoned that implicit in the jury determination was that the 5.7 percent salary increase was a substitute for the lost pension and that defendant's contractual obligation was to pay the pre-Measure 8 salaries plus a six percent pension contribution. Under Or. Rev. Stat. § 652.615, which allowed recovery of actual damages, setting damages on the wage claim based on the contract damages was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

565 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoin


A115646


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


190 Ore. App. 532; 79 P.3d 342; 2003 Ore. App. LEXIS 1540


August 27, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
November 13, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. McCoin, 336 Ore. 422, 2004 Ore. LEXIS 122 (Or., Feb. 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court, Crook County. Gary Thompson, Judge. MI000250.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Crook County, Oregon, convicted defendant for driving under the influence of intoxicants (DUII), treated defendant's six previous misdemeanor DUII convictions as three felony convictions, and sentenced defendant to 27 months' imprisonment under the sentencing guidelines grid. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, as a matter of statutory construction, Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.012(2) had to be interpreted to provide that the previous convictions that were a necessary element of the felony DUII charge were not also counted in his criminal history score. The appellate court noted that, by its terms, the statute provided that, in determining the criminal history score of persons convicted of felony DUII, the court had to consider every two previous misdemeanor DUII convictions to be equivalent to one person felony conviction. It did not contemplate exclusion of the first three convictions from a defendant's criminal history score. Nor did Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.010(5) provide contextual evidence of a different legislative intent. Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.012(2) unambiguously provided that all previous DUII convictions had to be counted in a defendant's criminal history score. The statute did not impose a separate punishment for defendant's prior DUII offenses in violation of the Fifth Amendment or Or. Const. art. I, § 12. The dual consideration of defendant's previous convictions in determining his punishment did not offend the protections against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
